The condition is fulfilled by completing the fast from dawn to sunset. The divorce occurs at the moment of sunset, not at the beginning of the fast.

Conditional Divorce on Childbirth: Cumulative Effect of Multiple Conditions
Ruling on cumulative conditional divorces

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the number of divorces when a husband makes conditional divorces tied to the gender of the child and the wife gives birth to twins (a boy and a girl).

Core Idea
When both conditions are fulfilled, all divorces are cumulative: one for the boy plus two for the girl equals three divorces.

In Hanafi fiqh, a husband may attach specific numbers of divorces to different conditions. When those conditions are simultaneously fulfilled, the divorces accumulate. This lesson examines a classic scenario where a husband ties one divorce to the birth of a boy and two divorces to the birth of a girl, and the wife delivers both twins.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conditions
The husband made two separate conditional statements: one for a boy (one divorce) and one for a girl (two divorces). Each condition is distinct and operates independently.
2
Note the number of divorces attached to each
The first condition triggers one divorce if a boy is born. The second condition triggers two divorces if a girl is born.
3
Determine if both conditions can be fulfilled
Since the wife gives birth to both a boy and a girl, both conditions are met simultaneously. There is no contradiction because the conditions are not mutually exclusive.
4
Apply the cumulative principle
Hanafi law treats multiple fulfilled conditions as cumulative. The total divorces are the sum: one (for the boy) plus two (for the girl) equals three divorces.
This is consistent with the general Hanafi rule that conditional talâq takes effect when the condition is fulfilled, and multiple conditions are honored if all are met.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شوہر نے بیوی سے کہا اذا ولدت غلاما فانت طالق واحدة واذا ولدت جارية فانت طالق ثنتین لڑکا اور لڑکی دوئوں کو جنا کتنی طلاقیں واقع ہونگی
The husband said to his wife: 'If you give birth to a male slave (boy), you are divorced one time, and if you give birth to a female slave (girl), you are divorced two times.' She gave birth to both a boy and a girl. How many divorces will occur?
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage presents a conditional divorce scenario where the husband attaches different numbers of divorces to the birth of a boy (one divorce) versus a girl (two divorces). When the wife gives birth to twins, both conditions are fulfilled. The Hanafi ruling is that both conditions apply, resulting in a total of three divorces (one for the boy and two for the girl). This demonstrates how multiple conditions are treated cumulatively.

Key Terms
غلام (ghulam): A male child; in context, a boy.
جارية (jariyah): A female child; in context, a girl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Two
C) Three

Key Takeaway
When multiple conditional divorces are fulfilled simultaneously, the divorces are cumulative unless a specific condition explicitly overrides others.

Conditional Divorce with Multiple Conditions and Bain Intervening
Ruling on multiple conditions with intervening bain divorce and remarriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a conditional divorce with multiple sub-conditions is triggered when the last sub-condition is fulfilled during a valid marriage, even if earlier sub-conditions occurred outside the marriage, using the example of speaking to two named individuals.

Core Idea
A conditional divorce fires when the final required action occurs inside the marriage.

The first scenario presents a husband who suspends three divorces on his wife speaking to two specific men. He then gives her a bain divorce. She speaks to one man while not his wife, later they remarry, and she speaks to the second while married. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi position that the three divorces occur upon the second speech, even though the first speech was outside the marriage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition and its structure
The husband said: 'If you speak to Abu Amr and Abu Yusuf, you are divorced thrice.' This is a conjunctive condition requiring both speeches.
The condition uses 'and' (و), so both sub-conditions must occur for the condition to be fulfilled.
2
Trace the marital timeline
The husband gave one bain divorce, ending the marriage. The wife's iddah passed. Then she spoke to Abu Amr while not married. Then they remarried. Then she spoke to Abu Yusuf while married.
Bain divorce makes the marriage irretrievable; remarriage requires a new contract.
3
Apply the rule on marital status for condition fulfillment
In Hanafi fiqh, a suspended divorce is only triggered if the condition is fulfilled during a valid marriage. The first speech occurred outside the marriage, so it is disregarded. The second speech occurred inside the marriage.
The first speech is considered legally irrelevant for the condition.
4
Determine the effect
Since the second speech completes the condition (the first is as if it never happened), the suspended triple divorce is triggered at the moment she speaks to Abu Yusuf while married.
The condition is considered fulfilled even though one sub-condition was performed outside marriage.
5
State the ruling
Three divorces occur, making her totally divorced and haram for the husband until she marries another and that marriage is consummated and she divorces (halala).
This is consistent with the quiz answer of three divorces.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(Third scenario): The husband said: 'If you enter the house, you are divorced thrice,' then said: 'You are divorced thrice.' She married another, he consummated, then she returned to the first husband and entered the house. Nothing occurs.

Commentary
This passage presents multiple intricate scenarios involving conditional divorces with intervening divorces and remarriages. The first scenario involves a condition to speak to two specific men. The second scenario: conditional on entering the house with intervening marriage to another and return. These illustrate the Hanafi rules on how intervening bain divorce and subsequent marriage affect conditional divorce.

Key Terms
بائنہ (bainah): Irrevocable divorce that ends the marriage immediately; remarriage requires a new contract.
عدت (iddah): Waiting period after divorce before remarriage.
تعلیق (ta'liq): Suspension of a divorce pronouncement on a condition.

Effect of Intervening Marriage on Suspended Conditional Divorce
Ruling on conditional divorce with intervening remarriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that a suspended conditional divorce is annulled when the marriage ends, and an intervening full divorce and subsequent remarriage do not revive the original condition, using the scenarios of house entry.

Core Idea
A suspended divorce dies with the marriage; remarriage cannot revive it.

The second and third scenarios involve a husband who suspends triple divorce on his wife entering a house. He then either gives some divorces or immediately pronounces three divorces. She marries another, consummates, divorces, returns, and enters the house. This lesson explains why no divorce occurs: the original marriage ended, cancelling the suspension, and the new marriage is a clean slate.

Guided Path
1
Differentiate the two sub-scenarios
In the second scenario, the husband says: 'If you enter the house, you are thrice divorced,' and then gives some divorces (likely enough to end the marriage). In the third, he says the condition and then immediately pronounces 'You are thrice divorced.'
The second scenario does not specify the number of divorces given, but the marriage ends as a result.
2
Determine the status of the marriage after the husband's actions
In both sub-scenarios, the husband's actions (giving divorces or pronouncing three) end the marriage. In the second, the divorces (whether one bain or two) end the marriage. In the third, the immediate triple pronouncement ends the marriage irrevocably.
After a triple divorce, the wife becomes haram until she marries another (halala). After a bain divorce (one or two if no consummation?), the marriage is also ended.
3
Apply the rule that a suspended divorce is cancelled when the marriage ends
The condition 'enter the house' was not fulfilled before the marriage ended. In Hanafi law, a suspended (mu'allaq) divorce is tied to the original marriage; once the marriage ends, the suspension is annulled.
This is similar to the concept that a suspended divorce cannot survive the dissolution of the marriage.
4
Consider the effect of remarriage
She marries another man (with consummation) and then divorces him, making her halal for the first husband. She returns to the first husband in a new marriage. The original conditional divorce was from the old marriage and is gone.
The new marriage is independent; no condition from the old marriage transfers unless renewed.
5
Conclude the ruling
When she enters the house in the new marriage, the condition from the old marriage is not applicable. Hence, no divorce occurs. The third scenario explicitly states 'nothing occurs'.
The second scenario, though not explicitly answered in the passage, follows the same principle: no divorce occurs.

After one divorce (making her bain), she speaks to the first man while not in marriage, then they remarry, then she speaks to the second man while married. The Hanafi ruling is that speaking to the second man while married triggers the three divorces (since the condition was 'if you speak to Abu Amr and Abu Yusuf...' both sub-conditions must be fulfilled while in marriage). The second scenario: conditional on entering the house with intervening marriage to another and return. The third scenario: similar but with an additional pronouncement, resulting in no occurrence due to the intervening marriage. These illustrate the Hanafi rules on how intervening bain divorce and subsequent marriage affect conditional divorce.

Key Terms
تعلیق (ta'liq): Suspension of a divorce pronouncement on a condition.
طلاق بائن (talaq bain): Irrevocable divorce that ends the marriage immediately; remarriage requires a new contract.
حلالہ (halala): The process by which a woman divorced three times becomes permissible to her first husband by marrying another man, consummating, and divorcing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the third scenario from the passage, what happens when the woman enters the house after returning from her second marriage?
A) Three divorces occur
B) One divorce occurs
C) Nothing occurs
D) Two divorces occur

Key Takeaway
A suspended conditional divorce is annulled when the marriage ends; remarriage does not revive the condition, so no divorce occurs from fulfilling the condition in a new marriage.

Conditional Divorce upon Intercourse and the Dower Obligation
Ruling on conditional divorce upon intercourse with dower details

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when a conditional divorce takes effect upon intercourse and when the full dower (mahr) becomes obligatory.

Core Idea
Triple divorce occurs at khitan contact; full dower requires withdrawal and re-entry.

This passage presents a specific scenario: a husband makes a conditional divorce dependent on intercourse. The ruling clarifies the precise moment the divorce becomes effective and the conditions under which the full dower is owed. Understanding these details prevents confusion in real-life marital negotiations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition and its trigger
The husband says: 'When I have intercourse with you, you have three divorces.' The condition is 'when I have intercourse.' The trigger is the actual act of intercourse.
The condition is fulfilled by the action itself, not just the intention.
2
Determine when divorce occurs
The passage states that as soon as the two circumcised parts meet (iltiqa al-khitanayn), the triple divorce occurs. This is the Hanafi criterion for full intercourse.
This is the same criterion used for ghusl obligation.
3
Understand the dower ruling in the 'staying' scenario
If the husband remains inside for even a moment after penetration, the divorce occurs but the full dower is not obligatory. This indicates that mere penetration without further action does not trigger the mahr obligation.
The passage says 'if he remained for a moment, dower is not wajib.'
4
Understand the dower ruling in the 'withdrawal and re-entry' scenario
If the husband withdraws and then re-enters, the full dower becomes obligatory. The repetition of the act triggers the dower obligation.
This suggests that full mahr is tied to repeated or deliberate acts, not just initial contact.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شوہر نے بیوی سے کہا۔ جب میں تجھ سے جماع کروں تجھے تین طلاق اس نے جماع کیا پس جب التقاء ختانین ہوا تو تین طلاق واقع ہو جائیں گی اگر ایک گھڑی پڑا رہا تو مہر واجب نہیں اگر نکالا پھر داخل کیا تو مہر واجب ہے
The husband said to his wife: 'When I have intercourse with you, you have three divorces.' He had intercourse. So when the two circumcised parts meet, three divorces occur. If he remained (inside) for a moment, the dower is not obligatory; if he withdrew then re-entered, the dower is obligatory.
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This ruling addresses conditional divorce upon intercourse. The moment the two circumcised parts (khitan) meet, the condition is fulfilled, and three divorces occur. Then it discusses the obligation of dower (mahr): if the husband remains inside for even a short time, no mahr is due (because the act is incomplete regarding mahr obligation?), but if he withdraws and re-enters, then the full mahr becomes wajib. This reflects Hanafi rules on mahr obligation being tied to full penetration or repeated actions.

Key Terms
التقاء ختانین (iltiqa al-khitanayn): The meeting of the two circumcised parts, i.e., the genitals, indicating actual penetration.
مہر (mahr): Dower, obligatory payment from husband to wife upon marriage or consummation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Triple divorce occurs but no dower
C) No divorce occurs
D) Only one divorce occurs

Key Takeaway
In conditional divorce upon intercourse, the divorce takes effect at khitan contact, but full dower is only wajib if the husband withdraws and re-enters.

Exception (Istithna) in Divorce: Insha'Allah and Numeric Exceptions
Ruling on using exceptions (istithna) in divorce pronouncements

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on exception in divorce and apply them to given scenarios involving 'insha'Allah' and numeric exceptions.

Core Idea
In Hanafi law, immediate exception (istithna) in divorce reduces the count; 'insha'Allah' negates the divorce entirely.

Divorce is a serious matter, and the precise wording matters. The Hanafi school recognizes that a husband may attach exceptions to his pronouncement, either suspending it with 'insha'Allah' or reducing the number with 'illa'. This lesson covers two clear rules: the effect of saying 'insha'Allah' immediately, and how numeric exceptions work.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of exception
Determine whether the pronouncement includes a suspensive condition (insha'Allah) or a subtractive exception (illa followed by a number).
2
Apply the rule for suspensive exception
If the husband says 'You are divorced, if Allah wills' immediately without pause, no divorce occurs. The condition negates the intent.
Immediacy is crucial; a pause would make the divorce effective.
3
Apply the rule for subtractive exception
If the husband says 'You are divorced thrice except one', subtract the exception number from the total. Two divorces occur.
The exception must be part of the same utterance.
4
Verify conditions
Ensure any required conditions (immediacy for insha'Allah, same sentence for illa) are met.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
استثناء کا بیان شوہر نے بیوی کو انت طالق ان شاء الله متصلاً کہا تو طلاق واقع نہیں ہوگی شوہر نے منکوحہ سے کہا انت طالق ثلاثا الا واحدۃ تو دو طلاقیں واقع ہوں گی اور اگر کہا انت طالق ثلاثا الا ثنتین تو ایک طلاق واقع ہوگی
Section on exception (istithna). If the husband says to his wife: 'You are divorced, if Allah wills,' immediately, then divorce does not occur. If the husband says to his wife: 'You are divorced thrice except one,' then two divorces occur. And if he says: 'You are divorced thrice except two,' then one divorce occurs.
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage establishes the Hanafi rules for istithna (exception) in divorce. Two types of exceptions are presented: 1. Taliq (suspension) using 'insha'Allah' – if said immediately without pause, the divorce is not affected because it is considered as leaving the matter to God's will, which negates the intention. 2. Istithna using 'illa' – if one says 'three except one', two divorces are counted; if 'except two', one divorce occurs. The exception reduces the number of divorces by the stated amount. This is based on the linguistic principle that exception from a number subtracts the exception.

Key Terms
استثناء (istithna): Exception; a linguistic or legal exclusion that subtracts from or qualifies a statement.
ان شاء الله (insha'Allah): If Allah wills; used as a suspensive condition that invalidates the divorce if said immediately.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a husband says 'You are divorced thrice except one', how many divorces occur?
A) Three
B) Two
C) One
D) None

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, immediate exception with 'insha'Allah' voids the divorce, while numeric exception subtracts from the count.

Mut'ah (Consolatory Gift) for Divorced Women
Ruling that mut'ah is mustahabb for all divorced women except one specific type.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mut'ah, identify the exception, and explain the disagreement with the Shafi'i school.

Core Idea
Mut'ah is recommended for every divorced woman except the one who already receives half the mahr.

In this lesson, we examine the legal status of mut'ah — a consolatory gift given by a husband to his divorced wife. The Hanafi school holds that mut'ah is mustahabb (recommended) for all divorced women except one specific case, while the Shafi'i school argues it is wajib (obligatory) in most circumstances. Understanding this dispute clarifies the practical difference in how judges from each school would rule.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling given in the matn: mut'ah is mustahabb (recommended) for every divorced woman except one.
The exception is crucial.
2
Identify the exception
Find the woman for whom mut'ah is not recommended: she who is divorced before consummation and for whom a mahr was specified.
Because she receives half the mahr, which serves as consolation.
3
Contrast with the Shafi'i position
State Imam al-Shafi'i's view: mut'ah is wajib for every divorced woman except that same exception.
The exception is agreed upon, but the general ruling differs.
4
Analyze the proof and practical consequence
Consider the dalil each school uses: Hanafis see mut'ah as a substitute (khalaf) while Shafi'is see it as an original obligation. Note the thamarah al-khilaf: enforceability in court.
Hanafi judge does not enforce mut'ah; Shafi'i judge would.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وتستحب المتعة لكل مطلقة المطلقة واحدة وهى التى طلقها الزوج قبل الدخول بها وقد سمى لهامهرا وقال الشافعى تجب لكل مطلقة الالهذه لانها وجبت صلة من الزوج لانه او حشها بالفراق في هذه الصورة نصف المهر طريقة المتعة لان الطلاق فسخ فى هذه الحالة والمتعة لاتتكرر ولنا ان المتعة خلف
He said: Mut'ah is recommended for every divorced woman except one: she whom the husband divorced before consummation and for whom he specified a mahr. And al-Shafi'i said: It is obligatory for every divorced woman except this one, because it became a gift from the husband since he made her sad by separation. In this case, half the mahr takes the place of mut'ah, because divorce here is a dissolution, and mut'ah does not repeat. And we have that mut'ah is a substitute...
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage begins a new section on mut'ah (consolatory gift) for a divorced woman. The matn states that mut'ah is mustahabb (recommended) for every divorced woman except one: a woman divorced before consummation whose mahr was specified in the contract. For such a woman, the half mahr she receives serves as the mut'ah. Imam al-Shafi'i opines that mut'ah is obligatory (wajib) for every divorced woman except this category. The Hanafi position (indicated by 'we have') is that mut'ah is a substitute (khalaf) for something else—likely a substitute for the full mahr when it is not due. The reasoning: in the case of divorce before consummation with a specified mahr, the half mahr fulfills the purpose of consolation. The text cuts off during the Hanafi argument.

Key Terms
المتعة (al-mut'ah): A consolatory gift given by the husband to the divorced wife, usually as a form of comfort.
المطلقة (al-mutallaqa): A woman divorced by her husband.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) A woman divorced before consummation whose mahr was not specified.
D) A woman divorced after the mahr was paid in full.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds mut'ah is mustahabb for all divorced women except the one who receives half mahr as consolation; the Shafi'i school holds it is wajib for all except that case.

Hanafi Response to Shafi'i's Argument for Wajib Mut'ah
Response to Shafi'i's proof that mut'ah is wajib after divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on mut'ah and evaluate why it is mustahabb not wajib, using the argument that the husband is not a wrongdoer.

Core Idea
Mut'ah is mustahabb because divorce is permitted; the husband is not a jani.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi response to Imam al-Shafi'i's claim that mut'ah (post-divorce compensation) is wajib. The author of al-Hidayah argues that the husband, acting with shari'ah permission, is not considered a wrongdoer (jani), and therefore mut'ah remains a recommended act of kindness, not a mandated penalty.

Guided Path
1
State the issue
What is mut'ah and what is the core dispute between Hanafi and Shafi'i schools?
Mut'ah is a post-divorce gift; Shafi'i says wajib, Hanafi says mustahabb.
2
Identify the Shafi'i proof
Why does Imam al-Shafi'i hold that mut'ah is wajib? Identify the basis of his argument.
He argues that divorce causes distress (wahsha) to the woman, so compensation is due.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
How does the Hanafi school rebut this? Focus on the concept of 'jani' (wrongdoer) and shari'ah permission.
The husband is not a wrongdoer because he acts within the bounds set by shari'ah.
4
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical difference in ruling between wajib and mustahabb?
In Hanafi, mut'ah is optional; in Shafi'i, it is obligatory.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Why is the Hanafi position considered mufta bihi (the relied-upon view) in this text?
The text treats the Hanafi position as correct, citing logical consistency.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مدخول بہا سمی لہا کیلئے متعہ واجب کیا گیا تو خلیفہ کا جزو اصل یعنی نصف مہر کے ساتھ جمع ہونا لازم آئے گا اور یہ سب صورتیں خلاف ضابطہ ہیں۔ اسلئے ان تینوں صورتوں میں متعہ واجب نہیں ہوگا۔ وهو غير جان سے صاحب ہدایہ نے امام شافعی کی دلیل کا جواب دیا ہے۔ جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ یہ تو تسلیم ہے کہ عورت کو فراق کی وجہ سے وحشت میں ڈال دیا۔ لیکن اس ایجاش میں وہ جانی یعنی جنایت کرنے والا نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ شریعت نے اس کو طلاق دینے کی اجازت دی ہے۔ بلکہ بعض چھورتوں میں طلاق دینا مستحب ہے۔ مثلاً جبکہ عورت تارک الصلوۃ ہو اور سمجھانے پر شوہر کی اطاعت نہ کرتی ہو۔ پس جو عمل شریعت کی اجازت سے حاصل ہو گا اس کا کرنے والا جانی شمار نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ لہذا جب شوہر نے طلاق دے کر کوئی جنایت نہیں کی تو اس پر طلاق دے کر وحشت میں ڈالنے کی وجہ سے تاوان بھی واجب نہیں ہو گا۔ پس یہ متعہ باب احسان کے قبیلہ سے ہوگا۔ تاوان کے قبیلہ سے نہیں۔ پس اس کو مستحب تو کہا جا سکتا ہے واجب نہیں کہا جا سکتا لہذا امام شافعی کا ان صورتوں میں متعہ کو واجب قرار دینا درست نہیں ہے۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب
When for a woman who has been consummated and whose mahr was named, mut'ah is made wajib, then the successor's part of the principle, i.e., half of the mahr, would have to be combined, and all these forms are contrary to the rule. Therefore in these three cases mut'ah is not wajib. And 'he is not a wrongdoer' - the author of Hidayah has responded to Imam Shafi'i's proof. The summary of the response is that it is conceded that the woman is thrown into distress due to separation. But in this distress, he is not a wrongdoer (jani), i.e., a criminal, because shari'ah has permitted him to give divorce. Rather, in some situations divorce is mustahabb, for example when the woman is neglectful of prayer and does not obey her husband despite admonition. So an act that occurs with shari'ah's permission, its doer is not considered a wrongdoer. Therefore when the husband did not commit any crime by giving divorce, compensation is not wajib upon him for causing distress by divorce. So this mut'ah is from the category of ihsan (benevolence), not from the category of penalty. So it can be called mustahabb, not wajib. Hence Imam Shafi'i's declaring mut'ah wajib in these cases is not correct. And Allah knows best what is correct.
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage is a response to Imam Shafi'i's argument that mut'ah (post-divorce compensation) is wajib because the husband causes distress. The Hanafi position, as stated by the author of Hidayah, is that mut'ah is mustahabb (recommended) but not wajib. The key point is that the husband is not considered a wrongdoer (jani) because he is acting with shari'ah permission. Divorce is allowed, and in some cases even recommended. Therefore, the distress caused is not actionable as a tort, and mut'ah remains a voluntary act of kindness (ihsan) rather than a mandated penalty. The passage addresses three specific cases where mut'ah would not be wajib, but then focuses on the general principle.

Key Terms
متعہ (mut'ah): Post-divorce compensation given to the woman as a gesture of kindness.
جانی (jani): Wrongdoer or criminal who commits a transgression.
وحشت (wahsha): Distress or emotional pain caused by separation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi response, why is mut'ah not wajib?
A) Because the husband is a jani
B) Because the husband acts with shari'ah permission
C) Because the woman is at fault
D) Because mut'ah is not mentioned in Quran

Key Takeaway
Mut'ah is mustahabb, not wajib, because the husband acts with shari'ah permission and is not a wrongdoer.

Introduction to Kitab al-Talaq: Definition and Types of Divorce
Defining talaq and classifying its types: Ahsan, Hasan, Bid'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of talaq and distinguish between Ahsan, Hasan, and Bid'i divorce based on their conditions.

Core Idea
Ahsan divorce: one revocable divorce in a clean period without intercourse—furthest from regret and most preferred.

Divorce (talaq) is a serious act in Islamic law with specific rules to prevent harm and regret. The Hanafi school classifies talaq into types based on how and when it is pronounced. This lesson unpacks the definition of talaq and its three categories as presented in al-Hidayah, focusing on the conditions that make Ahsan the best practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the lexical and Shar'i definition of talaq
Read the text that defines talaq in language ('removing a restriction absolutely') and in Shari'ah ('removing the marriage tie through specific words'). Note that both definitions emphasize removal of a bond.
The arabic_clean includes a lexical note from al-Mughrib.
2
Break down the three types of talaq
The matn states talaq is of three types: Hasan, Ahsan, and Bid'i. Recognize that Ahsan and Hasan are both Sunní (conforming to Sunnah), while Bid'i is innovative. Ahsan is the best; Hasan is good but different in timing.
The text only defines Ahsan in detail; Hasan and Bid'i are named but not fully described here.
3
Extract the conditions of Ahsan divorce
The text specifies: (1) one divorce, (2) in a state of purity (tuhr) when the husband has not had intercourse with her, (3) then leaving her until her iddah expires. Identify each condition precisely.
The condition is on the husband not having intercourse in that tuhr, not on the woman's state per se.
4
Understand the rationale for Ahsan being the best
The Companions preferred this method because it minimizes regret and harm to the woman. The text mentions two reasons: farthest from regret, least harmful. Also, there is no disagreement that Ahsan is not disliked (karahah).
The phrase 'لا خلاف لاحد في الكراهة' is interpreted to mean no one considers it disliked; i.e., it is commendable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کتاب الطلاق
ترجمہ یہ کتاب طلاق کے بیان میں ہے
باب طلاق السنة
ترجمہ یہ باب طلاق سنت کے بیان میں ہے
مصنف علیہ الرحمۃ احکام نکاح سے فراغت کے بعد طلاق اور اس کے اقسام و احکام کو بیان فرمار ہے ہیں۔ چونکہ نکاح وجود میں سابق ہے اور طلاق لاحق اسلئے تعلیم میں بھی مصنف نے نکاح کے احکام پہلے بیان فرمائے اور طلاق کے احکام بعد میں ۔ طلاق کو رضاعت کے بعد ذکر کرنے کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ یہ دونوں موجب حرمت ہیں۔ مگر رضاعت سے حرمت موبدہ ثابت ہوتی ہے۔ اور طلاق سے غیر موبدہ پس صاحب ہدایہ نے حکم اشد ( رضاعت کے احکام) کو پہلے ذکر کیا اور حکم اخف ( طلاق کے احکام ) کو بعد میں ۔ مغرب میں ہے کہ طلاق . مصدر ہے تطلیق کے معنی میں ۔ جیسے سلام تسلیم کے معنی اور کلام تحکیم کے معنی میں ۔ لغت میں طلاق کہتے ہیں مطلقا قید اٹھانا اور شریعت کی اصلاح میں کہتے ہیں کہ قید نکاحی کو مخصوص الفاظ کے ذریعہ اٹھانا۔ پھر طلاق کی دو قسمیں ہیں۔ طلاق سنی اور طلاق بدگی ۔ پھر سنی کی دو قسمیں ہیں ۔ سنی من حیث العدد اور سنی من حیث الوقت۔ پھر سنی من حیث العدد کی دو قسمیں ہیں۔ حسن اور احسن : اور بدعی کی بھی دو قسمیں ہیں۔ بدگی من حیث العدد اور بدعی من حیث الوقت ۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے متفرق طریقہ سے ان تمام انواع و اقسام کو ذکر فرمایا ہے ۔
طلاق کی تین قسمیں
قال الطلاق على ثلثة اوجه حسن و احسین و بدعى فالاحسن ان يطلق الرجل امرأته تطليقة واحدة في طهر لم يجامعها فيه ويتركها حتى تنقضى عدتها لان للصحابة كانوا يستحبون ان لا يزيدوا في الطلاق على واحدة حتى تنقضى العدة و ان هذا افضل عندهم من ان يطلق الرجل ثلثاً عند كل ظهر واحدة ولانه ابعد من الندامة واقل ضرر بالمرأة و لا خلاف لاحد في الكراهة

(۲) احسن
بدگی
پس احسن یہ ہے کہ مرد اپنی بیوی کو ایک طلاق دے اپنے طہر میں جس میں جماع نہیں کیا اور عورت کو چھوڑے یہاں تک کہ اس کی عدت گذر جائے ۔ کیونکہ صحابہ رضوان اللہ علیہم اجمعین پسند کرتے تھے کہ طلاق میں ایک پر زیادہ نہ کریں یہاں تک کہ عدت گذر جائے۔ اور یہ بات ان کے نزدیک افضل تھی بمقابلہ اس نے کہ مرد تین طلاق دے ہر طہر پر ایک۔ اور اسلئے کہ یہ طلاق ندامت سے بہت دور ہے
اور عورت کے حق میں ضرر میں بہت کم ہے۔ اور کراہت کے بارے میں کسی کا اختلاف نہیں ( کراہت کا قائل کوئی نہیں)۔ تشریح صاحب قدوری نے طلاق کی تین قسمیں بیان فرما کر طلاق احسن کی تعریف کی ہے۔ چنانچہ فرمایا کہ طلاق احسن یہ ہے کہ مرد اپنی منکوحہ کو ایک طلاق ایسے طہر میں دے جس میں اس کے ساتھ جماع نہیں کیا ہے اور اس کو چھوڑے رکھے یہاں تک کہ اس کی عدت
Book of Divorce. Translation: This book is about the explanation of divorce. Chapter of the Sunnah Divorce. Translation: This chapter is about the explanation of the Sunnah divorce. The author (may Allah have mercy on him) after finishing the rulings of marriage, now explains divorce and its types and rulings. Since marriage precedes in existence and divorce follows, therefore in teaching the author first mentioned the rulings of marriage and then the rulings of divorce. The reason for mentioning divorce after fosterage is that both cause prohibition. However, fosterage establishes permanent prohibition, and divorce establishes non-permanent prohibition. So the author of Hidayah first mentioned the stronger ruling (fosterage rulings) and then the lighter ruling (divorce rulings). In Mughrib it is stated that talaq is a verbal noun (masdar) with the meaning of tatliq (to divorce), like salam with the meaning of taslim, and kalam with the meaning of tahkim (judgment). Lexically, talaq means absolutely removing a restriction; and in the terminology of Shari'ah, it means removing the marriage tie through specific words. Then there are two types of talaq: talaq sunni and talaq bid'i. Then sunni has two types: sunni from the perspective of number and sunni from the perspective of time. Then sunni from the perspective of number has two types: hasan and ahsan. And bid'i also has two types: bid'i from the perspective of number and bid'i from the perspective of time. The author of Hidayah mentioned all these types and kinds in a scattered manner. Three types of divorce. He said: Divorce is of three types: hasan, ahsan, and bid'i. The ahsan is that a man divorces his wife once in a state of purity (tuhr) in which he did not have intercourse with her, and leaves her until her waiting period (iddah) expires, because the Companions (may Allah be pleased with them) preferred not to exceed one divorce until the iddah expired, and this was better in their view than a man divorcing three times, one at each tuhr. And because it is furthest from regret and least harmful to the woman. And there is no disagreement about its being disliked (or: no one considers it disliked). Translation: He said that divorce is of three types: (1) Hasan, (2) Ahsan, (3) Bid'i. So Ahsan is that a man gives one divorce to his wife in his tuhr (purity) in which he did not have intercourse with her, and leaves her until her iddah passes. Because the Companions liked not to exceed one in divorce until the iddah passed. And this was better in their view compared to a man giving three divorces, one at each tuhr. And because this divorce is far from regret and less harmful to the woman. And there is no disagreement about karahah (dislike) (i.e., no one considers it disliked). Explanation: The author of Quduri stated three types of divorce and defined ahsan. Thus he said: Ahsan divorce is that a man gives his married wife one divorce in a tuhr in which he did not have intercourse with her, and leaves her until her iddah...
Source pages p. 222

Commentary
This passage opens Kitab al-Talaq (Book of Divorce) in the Urdu commentary of Hidayah. It begins with a front matter explaining why the author placed divorce after fosterage: both cause prohibition, but fosterage is permanent (stronger) and divorce is temporary (lighter). Then the passage provides a lexical and Shar'i definition of talaq, followed by a classification. The main matn (from Quduri) states that divorce is of three types: Hasan, Ahsan, and Bid'i. The Ahsan form is defined as one divorce in a tuhr (clean period, not menstruation), without intercourse, then leaving the wife until her iddah expires. This was the practice of the Companions, and it is the best form because it minimizes regret and harm. The final phrase 'لا خلاف لاحد في الكراهة' is interpreted by the Urdu commentator to mean 'no one considers it disliked'—i.e., Ahsan is not disliked; rather it is commendable. The passage then notes that Imam Quduri similarly defined Ahsan. The text breaks off during the explanation of Quduri's definition. This lesson type is a definition and ruling, since it defines the legal term talaq and its subtypes, and presents the ruling that Ahsan is the preferred (mustahab) form.

Key Terms
طلاق (talaq): Legally: removing the marriage tie through specific words (e.g., 'I divorce you'). Lexically: removing a restriction absolutely.
طلاق سنی (talaq sunni): Divorce that conforms to the Sunnah in terms of timing and number.
احسن (ahsan): The best type of talaq: one revocable divorce in a non-menstrual period without intercourse, followed by completion of iddah.
حسن (hasan): A good type of talaq: one revocable divorce in each tuhr, making three divorces at separate clean periods.
بدعی (bid'i): Innovative divorce that violates Sunnah, e.g., divorcing during menstruation or giving all three divorces at one time.
عدت (iddah): Waiting period after divorce during which a woman cannot remarry; for non-pregnant women it is three menstrual cycles.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the definition of Ahsan divorce according to the text?
A) Three divorces given in one sitting.
B) One divorce given during a non-menstrual period without intercourse, followed by waiting period.
C) One divorce given during menstruation.
D) Two divorces given in consecutive clean periods.

Key Takeaway
Ahsan is the most recommended form of divorce in the Hanafi school, requiring one pronouncement in a clean period without intercourse, followed by the waiting period—minimizing regret and harm.

Talaq Ahsan: Definition and Hanafi Proof
Defines talaq ahsan and proves its preferability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define talaq ahsan, state its ruling as mustahabb, and identify its evidential basis from the practice of the Companions and the Quranic verse 65:1.

Core Idea
One divorce, one purity, one waiting period — the most recommended form.

This lesson clarifies the best form of divorce in Hanafi fiqh: talaq ahsan. It is defined by precise conditions and supported by both the practice of the Companions and rational reasoning. Understanding this helps a Muslim husband execute divorce in a way that minimizes harm and leaves the door open for reconciliation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is talaq ahsan? The passage defines it as one divorce in a tuhr without intercourse, then leaving the wife until her 'idda expires. The ruling is mustahabb (recommended), not wajib.
2
Locate the dalil
The main proof is the practice of the Companions (Sahaba) who preferred not to exceed one divorce until the 'idda expires. This is a form of ijma' of the Sahaba. A secondary proof is rational: it minimizes regret and harm.
The Quranic verse 65:1 is also cited as supporting the rationale.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the Sahaba practice prove preferability? The text states they 'used to prefer' (كانوا يستحبون). Their judicious choice indicates that talaq ahsan is the superior method, aligning with the spirit of the Quranic verse that encourages reconciliation.
The rational proof connects ahsan to the possibility of rectification (tadarak).
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is complete consensus (ijma') that talaq ahsan is not makruh. The disagreement arises only for talaq hasan, which Imam Malik considered bid'a, whereas Hanafis consider it permissible though less preferred.
This reinforces that ahsan is universally accepted.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position (mufta bihi) is that talaq ahsan is the most recommended form. This is based on the authority of al-Quduri and the consistent teaching of the school. No intra-Hanafi dispute exists.
Later Hanafi works like al-Hidayah uphold this.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الطلاق على ثلثة اوجه حسن و احسین و بدعى فالاحسن ان يطلق الرجل امرأته تطليقة واحدة في طهر لم يجامعها فيه ويتركها حتى تنقضى عدتها لان للصحابة كانوا يستحبون ان لا يزيدوا في الطلاق على واحدة حتى تنقضى العدة و ان هذا افضل عندهم من ان يطلق الرجل ثلثاً عند كل ظهر واحدة ولانه ابعد من الندامة واقل ضرر بالمرأة و لا خلاف لاحد في الكراهة تشریح صاحب قدوری نے طلاق کی تین قسمیں بیان فرما کر طلاق احسن کی تعریف کی ہے۔ چنانچہ فرمایا کہ طلاق احسن یہ ہے کہ مرد اپنی منکوحہ کو ایک طلاق ایسے طہر میں دے جس میں اس کے ساتھ جماع نہیں کیا ہے اور اس کو چھوڑے رکھے یہاں تک کہ اس کی عدت  گذر جائے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ صحابہ رضوان اللہ علیہم اجمعین اس بات کو پسند فرماتے تھے کہ ایک طلاق سے زائد نہ دیں ۔ اور دوسری دلیل عقلی یہ ہے کہ ایک طلاق واقع کرنا ندامت سے بھی بہت دور ہے اور عورت کو ضرر بھی بہت کم پہنچے گا۔ ندامت سے بعد تو اسلئے ہے کہ شوہر کیلئے تدارک کا امکان ہے کہ وہ عدت میں رجعت کر سکتا ہے اور عدت کے بعد بغیر حلالہ کے تجدید نکاح کر سکتا ہے اور ایسا کرنا جس میں تدارک کی گنجائش باقی رہے اللہ رب العتز کے نزدیک مستحسن ہے چنانچہ ارشاد ہے لعل الله يحدث بعد ذالک امرا اور ضر ر ا سلئے کم ہے کہ ایک طلاق پر اکتفاء کرنے کی صورت میں عورت پر عدت طویل نہیں ہوگی اور ایک سے زیادہ کی صورت میں بسا اوقات عدت طویل ہو جاتی ہے۔ مثلاً طلاق دی اور رجعت کر لی پھر طلاق دی اور رجعت کر لی۔ لہذا طلاق احسن کی عدم کراہت پر سب کا اتفاق ہے۔ اس کی کراہت کا کوئی قائل نہیں ہے بخلاف طلاق حسن کے اسلئے کہ اس میں امام مالک کا اختلاف ہے۔
He said: Divorce is of three types: hasan, ahsan, and bid'i. The ahsan is that a man divorces his wife one divorce in a state of purity in which he has not had intercourse with her, and he leaves her until her 'idda expires. Because the Companions used to prefer not to increase divorce beyond one until the 'idda expires, and this was better in their view than that a man divorces three times, one at each purity. And because it is farther from regret and less harmful to the woman. And there is no disagreement about its being non-reprehensible. Explanation: The author of al-Quduri, after mentioning three types of divorce, defined talaq ahsan. He said: Talaq ahsan is that a man gives his wife one divorce in a state of purity in which he has not had intercourse with her, and he leaves her until her 'idda expires. The proof is that the Companions used to prefer not to give more than one divorce. And the second proof is rational: effecting one divorce is far from regret and causes less harm to the woman. It is far from regret because the husband has the possibility of rectification: he can take her back in the 'idda, and after the 'idda he can renew the marriage without tahlil. And such an action in which there remains room for rectification is pleasing to Allah Almighty, as He said: 'Perhaps Allah will bring about after that something new' (Quran 65:1). And harm is less because in the case of one divorce the 'idda is not prolonged, whereas with more than one the 'idda sometimes becomes long, e.g., he divorces and takes her back, then divorces and takes her back. Therefore, there is consensus that talaq ahsan is not reprehensible. No one holds it to be makruh, unlike talaq hasan, because there is disagreement from Imam Malik.
Source pages p. 222

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof. The passage begins by citing al-Quduri's matn that divorce is three types: hasan, ahsan, and bid'i. It then defines talaq ahsan: one divorce pronounced during a state of purity (tuhr) in which no intercourse has occurred, followed by leaving the wife to complete her 'idda (waiting period). The proof is twofold: first, the practice of the Companions who preferred not to exceed one divorce until the 'idda expires, considering it better than divorcing one at each tuhr. Second, a rational argument: ahsan minimizes regret because the husband retains the option to take her back during the 'idda or remarry after without needing an intermediary (tahlil), as the Quranic verse 'Perhaps Allah will bring about after that something new' indicates. It also minimizes harm to the woman by avoiding a prolonged 'idda. Therefore, there is complete consensus (ijma') that talaq ahsan is not makruh; no one considers it reprehensible. This contrasts with talaq hasan, which Imam Malik considered a bid'a. The passage highlights that the Hanafi position is that talaq ahsan is the most commendable form.

Key Terms
طلاق احسن (talaq ahsan): A single divorce pronounced in a non-menstrual purity, followed by leaving the wife until the 'idda expires.
عدت (idda): The waiting period a woman must observe after divorce before she can remarry.
طهر (tuhr): State of purity from menstruation, specifically the period between two menses.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary proof that talaq ahsan is the best form of divorce?
A) The practice of the Sahaba who preferred one divorce
B) A hadith from the Prophet commanding it
C) Consensus of all scholars that it is wajib
D) The verse 'Divorce twice' (Quran 2:229)

Key Takeaway
Talaq ahsan is the most recommended form of divorce in Hanafi fiqh, defined by one divorce in a period of purity without intercourse, with the ruling based on the practice of the Companions and the rationale of minimizing regret and harm.

Talaq Hasan: The Hanafi Proof and the Dispute with Imam Malik
Defines talaq hasan and presents Hanafi proof against Maliki bid'a claim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of talaq hasan, explain the Hanafi proof from the hadith of Ibn Umar, and evaluate the Maliki objection based on default prohibition.

Core Idea
Three divorces in three purities is sunna because the Prophet explicitly permitted it; the need for release can recur.

This passage defines talaq hasan (also called talaq al-sunnah) and confronts the Maliki claim that it is a bid'a. The Hanafi school argues from the hadith of Ibn Umar, which explicitly allows one divorce per purity, and reasons that the need for divorce may recur with renewed desire. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to distinguish between ruling levels (sunnah vs. bid'a) and to apply textual proofs in ikhtilaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition and ruling
Locate the Hanafi definition of talaq hasan: three divorces in three separate purities for a consummated marriage. Note that it is called 'talaq al-sunnah' but here sunnah means permissible (mubah), not recommended.
The commentator clarifies that divorce is not an act of worship.
2
State the Maliki objection
Imam Malik holds that talaq hasan is a bid'a. His reasoning: the default of divorce is prohibition (hurma), permission exists only for the need of release, and one divorce suffices; additional divorces are unnecessary and thus innovations.
3
Extract the Hanafi proof from the hadith
The Hanafis cite the hadith of Ibn Umar: the Prophet said the sunnah is to wait for purity and then divorce one divorce per qur'. This is direct textual permission for one divorce per purity, refuting the Maliki claim of bid'a.
The Hanafi interpretation of qur' is tuhr (purity period).
4
Understand the secondary issue: timing of pronouncement
The passage discusses whether to pronounce the divorce at the beginning or end of the purity. The preferred view (azhar) is to divorce immediately upon purity to avoid the risk of intercourse delaying the divorce.
This is a minor furu' within the Hanafi school.
5
Synthesize the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Hanafis consider three divorces in three purities valid and permissible; Malikis would consider them invalid as a prohibited innovation and might restrict to one divorce if following their school.
This difference affects actual marital dissolution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والحسن هو طلاق السنة وهو ان يطلق المدخول بها ثلاثاً في ثلثة اطهار وقال مالك انه بدعة و لا يباح الا واحدة لان الاصل فى الطلاق هو الحظر والاباحة لحاجة الخلاص و قد اندفعت بالواحدة و لنا قوله عليه السلام في حديث ابن عمر ان السنة ان يستقبل الطهر استقبالا فيطلقها لكل قرء تطليقة ولان الحكم يدار على دليل الحاجة وهو الاقدام على الطلاق في زمان تجدد الرغبة وهو الطهر فالحاجة كالمتكررة نظراً الى دليلها ثم قيل الأولى ان يؤخر الايقاع الى اخر الطهر احترزاً عن طول العدة و الا ظهران يطلقها كما طهرت لانه لواخرر بما يجامعها و من قصده التطليق فيبتلى بالايقاع عقيب الرقاع تشریح مصنف نے طلاق حسن کا نام طلاق سنت امام مالک پر رد کرنے کیلئے رکھا ہے ورنہ طلاق احسن بالا تفاق سنت ہے۔ اور یہاں سنت سے مراد مباح ہے۔ کیونکہ طلاق فی نفسہ ایسی عبادت نہیں جس پر ثواب مرتب ہو۔ پس اب طلاق مسنون کے معنی یہ ہوں گے ایسی طلاق جس کا ثبوت سنت سے ہے اور اسکا مرتکب مستحق عتاب نہیں۔ طلاق حسن ( طلاق سنت) کی تعریف یہ ہے کہ شوہر اپنی منکوحہ مدخول بہا کو تین طہر میں تین طلاق دے۔ حضرت امام مالک فرماتے
And the hasan is the divorce of the Sunnah, and it is that he divorces the one with whom he has consummated marriage three times in three purities. And Malik said: It is an innovation (bid'a) and it is not permissible except one, because the original ruling regarding divorce is prohibition, and permissibility is due to the need for release, and that need is fulfilled by one. And our proof is his saying, peace be upon him, in the hadith of Ibn 'Umar: 'The Sunnah is that he waits for purity, then divorces her one divorce for each menstruation period.' And because the ruling revolves around the evidence of need, and that is proceeding to divorce at a time of renewed desire, which is purity. So the need is considered repeated, looking at its evidence. Then it is said: The best is to delay the divorce to the end of purity, to avoid lengthening the 'idda. And the more apparent is that he divorces her as soon as she becomes pure, because if he delays, he might have intercourse with her, and his intention is to divorce, so he will end up divorcing after intercourse. Explanation: The author named talaq hasan as 'talaq al-sunnah' in order to refute Imam Malik; otherwise, talaq ahsan is unanimously sunna. And here 'sunnah' means permissible (mubah), because divorce in itself is not an act of worship for which reward is given. So now the meaning of 'masnun' divorce is a divorce that is proven by the Sunnah and the one who performs it is not deserving of blame. The definition of talaq hasan (talaq al-sunnah) is that the husband divorces his wife with whom he has consummated marriage three times in three purities. Imam Malik says...
Source pages p. 223

Commentary
This is an inter-madhhab dispute. The passage defines talaq hasan (also called talaq al-sunnah) as three divorces in three separate purities (tuhr) for a woman with whom marriage has been consummated. Imam Malik argues that this is a bid'a (innovation) and only one divorce is permissible, because the default ruling for divorce is prohibition (hurma), and permission is granted only for the need of release from marriage; since one divorce achieves that need, further divorces are unnecessary and thus innovation. The Hanafi response (lana) is based on the hadith of Ibn Umar, where the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The Sunnah is that he waits for purity, then divorces her one divorce for each menstruation period (qur').' This hadith explicitly permits one divorce in each purity. Additionally, the Hanafis reason that the need for divorce recurs as desire renews at each purity; thus, the ruling (jawaz) is tied to the evidence of need, which is the renewed desire at each purity. Therefore, the need is considered recurring, and multiple divorces are allowed. Next, the passage discusses a subsidiary issue: whether to pronounce the divorce at the beginning or end of the purity. Some say it is better to delay to the end of the purity to avoid lengthening the 'idda, but the more apparent (azhar) view is to divorce as soon as she becomes pure, because delaying might lead to intercourse, which would defeat the purpose of divorce. The commentator explains that the author calls talaq hasan 'talaq al-sunnah' to refute Imam Malik's claim that it is bid'a. He clarifies that 'sunnah' here does not mean recommended (mustahabb) but legally permissible (mubah), as divorce is not an act of worship.

Key Terms
طلاق حسن (talaq hasan): Three divorces pronounced in three separate purities, for a woman with whom marriage has been consummated.
قرء (qur'): Menstruation period or the purity between two menses; in this hadith, it means the period of purity (tuhr).
بدعة (bid'a): An innovation in religion, considered blameworthy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is talaq hasan considered permissible despite the default prohibition of divorce?
A) Because the Quran states 'divorce is twice' (2:229)
B) Because the hadith of Ibn Umar explicitly permits one divorce per purity, establishing a specific sunnah
C) Because the Sahaba unanimously allowed it
D) Because divorce is always permissible

Key Takeaway
Talaq hasan (three divorces in three purities) is valid and permissible (mubah) in the Hanafi school, based on the explicit hadith of Ibn Umar, despite Imam Malik's classification of it as bid'a.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
12 min
Dispute with Imam Malik over Talaq Hasan (Talaq al-Sunnah)
Defining talaq hasan and debating its permissibility with Imam Malik

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on talaq hasan, state the Maliki objection, and evaluate the Hanafi proofs from hadith and rational argument.

Core Idea
Talaq hasan — three separate divorces in three tuhrs — is permissible (mubah) in the Hanafi school, contrary to Imam Malik who considers it bid'ah.

This lesson explores the Hanafi position on talaq hasan, a form of divorce where the husband gives three divorces over three purity periods (tuhr). Imam Malik considers this practice a bid'ah (innovation), arguing that only one divorce is permissible due to the original prohibition of divorce. The Hanafi school, however, relies on the explicit instruction of the Prophet ﷺ and a rational argument about repeated need to justify the permissibility of three divorces. Understanding this dispute clarifies the different methodologies in interpreting the sources of law.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what the Hanafi school holds regarding talaq hasan: it is the sunnah divorce, permissible (mubah), and not bid'ah.
The text defines talaq hasan as three divorces in three separate tuhr periods to a consummated wife.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam Malik holds that this practice is bid'ah and only one divorce is permissible. Understand his reasoning.
Malik's basis: the original ruling of divorce is prohibition (due to hadith 'Marry and do not divorce'), and permissibility is only for the need of release, which is fulfilled by one divorce.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine Malik's proof: the hadith 'Marry and do not divorce' indicates prohibition; permissibility is granted only as a concession for need, and one divorce suffices. Therefore, additional divorces are not justified.
This is a principle-based argument: al-asl fi al-talaq al-hazr (the origin of divorce is prohibition).
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school counters with two proofs: (a) the hadith of Ibn Umar where the Prophet instructed a divorce per tuhr, directly permitting multiple divorces; (b) a rational argument: the need for divorce is internal and judged by its external evidence (proceeding to divorce in a time of renewed desire, i.e., tuhr). If the evidence repeats, the need is considered repeated, justifying multiple divorces.
The Hanafi response shows that Malik's principle of original prohibition is overridden by the specific instruction of the Prophet and the reasoning about repeated need.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical difference: Hanafis allow up to three separate divorces over three tuhr periods; Malikis only permit one divorce in the marriage. This affects the number of divorces that are legally recognized.
This is a clear example of how different usul lead to different fiqh rulings.

اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو بدایہ جلد چهارم گذر جائے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ صحابہ رضوان اللہ علیہم اجمعین اس بات کو پسند فرماتے تھے کہ ایک طلاق سے زائد نہ دیں ۔ اور دوسری دلیل عقلی یہ ہے کہ ایک طلاق واقع کرنا ندامت سے بھی بہت دور ہے اور عورت کو ضرر بھی بہت کم پہنچے گا۔ ندامت سے بعد تو اسلئے ہے کہ شوہر کیلئے تدارک کا امکان ہے کہ وہ عدت میں رجعت کر سکتا ہے اور عدت کے بعد بغیر حلالہ کے تجدید نکاح کر سکتا ہے اور ایسا کرنا جس میں تدارک کی گنجائش باقی رہے اللہ رب العزت کے نزدیک مستحسن ہے چنانچہ ارشاد ہے لعل الله يحدث بعد ذالک امرا اور ضر ر ا سلئے کم ہے کہ ایک طلاق پر اکتفاء کرنے کی صورت میں عورت پر عدت طویل نہیں ہوگی اور ایک سے زیادہ کی صورت میں بسا اوقات عدت طویل ہو جاتی ہے۔ مثلاً طلاق دی اور رجعت کر لی پھر طلاق دی اور رجعت کر لی۔ لہذا

والحسن هو طلاق السنة وهو ان يطلق المدخول بها ثلاثاً في ثلثة اطهار وقال مالك انه بدعة و لا يباح الا واحدة لان الاصل فى الطلاق هو الحظر والاباحة لحاجة الخلاص و قد اندفعت بالواحدة و لنا قوله عليه السلام في حديث ابن عمر ان السنة ان يستقبل الطهر استقبالا فيطلقها لكل قرء تطليقة ولان الحكم يدار على دليل الحاجة وهو الاقدام على الطلاق في زمان تجدد الرغبة وهو الطهر فالحاجة كالمتكررة نظراً الى دليلها ثم قيل الأولى ان يؤخر الايقاع الى اخر الطهر احترزاً عن تطويل العدة و الا ظهران يطلقها كما طهرت لانه لواخرر بما يجامعها و من قصده التطليق فيبتلى بالايقاع عقيب الرقاع ترجمہ اور حسن وہ طلاق سنت ہے اور وہ یہ ہے کہ طلاق دے مدخول بہا کو تین ، تین طہر میں۔ اور امام مالک نے فرمایا کہ یہ بدعت ہے اور نہیں مباح ہے مگر ایک کیونکہ اصل طلاق میں ممانعت ہے۔ اور اباحت چھٹکارا پانے کی حاجت کی وجہ سے ہے۔ اور حاجت دفع ہو گئی ایک سے ۔ اور ہماری دلیل حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کا قول ہے حدیث ابن عمر میں کہ سنت یہ ہے کہ طہر کا انتظار کرے۔ پھر اس کو ہر طہر میں ایک طلاق دے۔ اور اسلئے کہ حکم دائر ہوتا ہے حاجت طلاق کی دلیل پر۔ اور وہ (دلیل) اقدام علی الطلاق ہے تجد در غبت کے زمانہ میں اور وہ ( تجدد رغبت کا زمانہ ) طہر ہے۔ پس حاجت متکررہ کے مانند ہوگئی دلیل حاجت کی طرف نظر کرتے ہوئے۔ پھر کہا گیا کہ ایقاع طلاق کو مؤخر کیا جائے طہر کے آخر تک تطویل عدت سے بچتے ہوئے ۔ اور اظہر یہ ہے کہ اس کو طلاق دے۔ جیسے ہی طہر (شروع) ہو۔ اسلئے کہ اگر مؤخر کرے گا تو بسا اوقات اس سے جماع کر لے گا۔ حالانکہ اس کا ارادہ طلاق دینے کا ہے۔ پس وہ مبتلا ہو جائے گا جماع کے بعد (طلاق) واقع کرنے کے ساتھ۔ تشریح مصنف نے طلاق حسن کا نام طلاق سنت امام مالک پر رد کرنے کیلئے رکھا ہے ورنہ طلاق احسن بالا تفاق سنت ہے۔ اور یہاں سنت سے مراد مباح ہے۔ کیونکہ طلاق فی نفسہ ایسی عبادت نہیں جس پر ثواب مرتب ہو۔ پس اب طلاق مسنون کے معنی یہ ہوں گے ایسی طلاق جس کا ثبوت سنت سے ہے اور اسکا مرتکب مستحق عتاب نہیں۔ طلاق حسن ( طلاق سنت) کی تعریف یہ ہے کہ شوہر اپنی منکوحہ مدخول بہا کو تین طہر میں تین طلاق دے۔ حضرت امام مالک فرماتے
ہیں کہ یہ طلاق بدعت ہے اور مباح صرف ایک طلاق ہے۔ امام مالک کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ طلاق میں ممانعت اصل ہے۔ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کے ارشاد تزوجوا ولا تطلقوا (رواہ ابوداؤد) کی وجہ سے یعنی نکاح کر دو اور طلاق مت دو۔ اور اباحت طلاق عورت سے چھٹکارا پانے کی حاجت کی وجہ سے ہے۔ اور حاجت ایک طلاق سے پوری ہو جاتی ہے۔ لہذا دوسری طلاق مباح نہیں ہوگی۔
اور ہماری دلیل حدیث ابن عمر ہے۔ حاصل حدیث یہ ہیکہ حضرت عبداللہ بن عمر نے حالت حیض میں اپنی بیوی کو طلاق دیدی۔ پھر ارادہ کیا کہ دوسری دو طلاقیں دو طہر میں دیدیں۔ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کو اس واقعہ کی خبر ہو گئی ۔ آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ اے ابن عمر ایسا کر نیکا تجھے اللہ نے حکم نہیں دیا تو سنت کو چوک گیا۔ سنت یہ ہے کہ تو انتظار کرے ظہر کا ۔ پھر ہر طہر میں طلاق دے۔ پھر مجھے حکم دیا تو میں نے اپنی بیوی سے رجعت کر لی۔ پھر آپ نے فرمایا کہ جب وہ پاک ہو جائے تو تو اسوقت طلاق دے یا روک لے۔ میں نے کہا اے اللہ کے رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم بتلائیے اگر میں اس کو تین طلاقیں دے دوں تو کیا میرے لیئے اس سے مراجعت کرنا حلال ہے۔ آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا نہیں وہ تو بائنہ ہوگئی اور گناہ ہو گیا یہ
حدیث دار قطنی کی روایت کردہ ہے۔ اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوتا ہیکہ متفرق طور پر تین طہر میں تین طلاقیں واقع کرنا سنت ہے۔ عقلی دلیل کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ حاجت طلاق امر باطن ہے۔ اس پر مطلع ہونا ناممکن ہے۔ لہذا حکم اس کی دلیل پر دائر کیا جائے گا۔ اور حاجت طلاق کی دلیل تجد در غبت یعنی طہر کے زمانہ میں طلاق دینے کا اقدام کرنا ہے۔ اور جب بھی دلیل حاجت میں تکرار ہو گا تو گویا حاجت الى الاطلاق میں تکرار ہوا۔ اور جب حاجت الی الطلاق میں تکرار ہے تو پھر تکرار طلاق بھی مباح ہوگا اسلئے ہماری رائے یہ ہے کہ متفرق طور پر تین طہر میں تین طلاقیں واقع کرنا مباح ہوگا۔
بدعت نہیں۔
Ashraf al-Hidaya, Urdu commentary of Hidaya, volume four. The proof is that the Companions (may Allah be pleased with them) liked that one should not give more than one divorce. And the second rational proof is that giving one divorce is far from regret and causes less harm to the woman. Far from regret because the husband has the possibility of rectification: he can take her back during the waiting period or renew the marriage without halala after the waiting period. Doing something that allows rectification is commendable to Allah Almighty, as He says: 'Perhaps Allah will bring about after that something new.' And the harm is less because if one is content with one divorce, the waiting period for the woman is not long, whereas with more than one, the waiting period sometimes becomes long. For example, he divorces and takes her back, then divorces and takes her back. Therefore, everyone agrees on the non-reprehensibility of talaq ahsan. No one holds it to be makruh, unlike talaq hasan because of the difference with Imam Malik. Talaq Hasan – Imam Malik's View. 'And al-hasan is the sunnah divorce, and it is that he divorces the one with whom he has consummated three times in three pure periods. Malik said: It is an innovation, and it is not permissible except one, because the origin in divorce is prohibition, and permissibility is due to the need for release, and that need has been fulfilled by one. Our proof is his statement, peace be upon him, in the hadith of Ibn Umar: The sunnah is that he should properly wait for purity and divorce her one divorce for each purity period. And because the ruling is based on the evidence of need, which is proceeding to divorce in a time of renewed desire, and that is the purity period. So the need becomes repeated, considering its evidence. Then it was said: It is better to delay the pronouncement to the end of the purity period, to avoid prolonging the waiting period. But the more apparent is that he divorces her when she becomes pure, because if he delays, he may have intercourse with her, while he intends divorce, and then he will be forced to pronounce divorce after intercourse.' Translation: And hasan is the sunnah divorce, and it is that he divorces the one with whom he has consummated three times in three purity periods. Imam Malik said: This is an innovation and it is not permissible except one, because the origin in divorce is prohibition. Permissibility is due to the need for release, and the need is fulfilled by one. Our proof is the statement of the Prophet (peace be upon him) in the hadith of Ibn Umar that the sunnah is to wait for purity and then give her one divorce for each purity period. And because the ruling is based on the evidence of need, which is proceeding to divorce in a time of renewed desire, and that is the purity period. So the need becomes like repeated, considering its evidence. Then it was said: The pronouncement should be delayed to the end of the purity period to avoid prolonging the waiting period. But the more apparent is that he divorces her as soon as she becomes pure, because if he delays, he may have intercourse with her while he intends divorce, and then he will be forced to pronounce divorce after intercourse. Commentary: The author has named talaq hasan as talaq sunnah to refute Imam Malik; otherwise, talaq ahsan is unanimously sunnah. Here, sunnah means permissible because divorce in itself is not an act of worship with reward. So the meaning of sunnah divorce is: a divorce proven by the sunnah, and the one who performs it is not deserving of blame. The definition of talaq hasan (sunnah divorce) is that the husband gives three divorces to his wife with whom he has consummated in three purity periods. Imam Malik says that this divorce is an innovation and only one divorce is permissible. Imam Malik's proof is that the original ruling on divorce is prohibition due to the Prophet's saying: 'Marry and do not divorce' (narrated by Abu Dawud), meaning marry and do not divorce. Permissibility of divorce is due to the need to be free from the woman, and the need is fulfilled by one divorce. Therefore, a second divorce is not permissible. Our proof is the hadith of Ibn Umar. The summary of the hadith is that Abdullah ibn Umar divorced his wife while she was menstruating. Then he intended to give two more divorces in two purity periods. The Prophet (peace be upon him) came to know of this and said: 'O Ibn Umar, Allah has not commanded you to do this. You have missed the sunnah. The sunnah is that you wait for purity and then give one divorce in each purity period.' Then he commanded me, so I took her back. Then the Prophet said: 'When she becomes pure, then either divorce her at that time or keep her.' I said: 'O Messenger of Allah, if I give her three divorces, will it be permissible for me to take her back?' The Prophet said: 'No, she becomes bain and a sin is incurred.' This hadith is narrated by Dar Qutni. This hadith shows that giving three divorces separately in three purity periods is sunnah. The sum of the rational proof is that the need for divorce is an internal matter; it is impossible to know it. Therefore, the ruling is based on its evidence. The evidence of need for divorce is the action of proceeding to divorce in a time of renewed desire, which is the purity period. Whenever this evidence is repeated, the need for divorce is regarded as repeated. And when the need for divorce is repeated, then repetition of divorce is also permissible. Therefore, our view is that giving three divorces separately in three purity periods is permissible, not an innovation.
Source pages p. 223

Commentary
This passage addresses the inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam Malik regarding talaq hasan (also called talāq al-sunnah). The author begins by noting unanimous agreement on the non-reprehensibility of talaq ahsan (a form where the husband gives one divorce per tuhr without revocation) and then introduces the point of contention: talaq hasan, which is three divorces given in three separate tuhr periods. The Arabic matn from al-Hidayah is presented, defining talaq hasan and noting that Imam Malik considers it bid'ah (blameworthy innovation) and only permits one divorce. Malik's reasoning: the original ruling for divorce is prohibition (based on the hadith 'Marry and do not divorce'), and permissibility exists only due to the need for release from the marriage; that need is satisfied by one divorce, so additional divorces are not permitted. The Hanafi proof consists of two parts: (1) A hadith from Abdullah ibn Umar (narrated by Dar Qutni), where the Prophet instructed him to divorce one per tuhr, which explicitly permits multiple divorces over time. (2) A rational argument: the need for divorce is internal and judged by its external evidence, which is the husband's action of proceeding to divorce during a time of renewed desire (i.e., purity). Since this action can be repeated, the need is considered repeated, and thus multiple divorces are justified. The Hanafi position is that such divorces are sunnah (here meaning mubah, permissible) and not bid'ah. The text also notes a secondary discussion among Hanafi mashāyikh about whether it is better to pronounce the divorce at the beginning or end of the purity period, with the more apparent (azhar) view being immediate pronouncement to avoid intercourse during the intended period of divorce.

Key Terms
طلاق حسن (talāq hasan): Divorce in accordance with the sunnah where the husband gives three divorces in three separate purity periods (tuhr) to a wife with whom he has consummated.
بدعة (bid‘ah): A blameworthy innovation in religious matters. Imam Malik labels talaq hasan as bid'ah.
سنة (sunnah): In this context, sunnah means mubah (permissible) because divorce is not an act of worship. It refers to a practice proven by the sunnah, not blameworthy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on giving three divorces in three separate tuhr periods (talaq hasan)?
A) It is haram and bid'ah.
B) It is makruh but permissible.
C) It is sunnah (mubah) and not bid'ah.
D) It is only permissible if the wife consents.

Key Takeaway
Talaq hasan is permissible (mubah) in the Hanafi school, not bid'ah, based on the Prophet's instruction to divorce one per tuhr and the principle that repeated evidence indicates repeated need.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
12 min
Hanafi Disagreement on Timing of Divorce within Tuhr
Discussing whether to pronounce divorce at beginning or end of the pure period.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the two Hanafi opinions on the optimal timing of talaq sunnah and identify the view preferred by the author of al-Hidayah.

Core Idea
Divorce at tuhr's end shortens iddah; immediate divorce avoids sunnah violation.

In this passage, the author of al-Hidayah presents a disagreement among Hanafi scholars regarding the best time to pronounce talaq sunnah within the woman's pure period. Both views are rooted in different concerns: one prioritizes shortening the waiting period, while the other prioritizes avoiding intercourse after the intention to divorce. Understanding this dispute illustrates how the Hanafi school accommodates valid internal differences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
The issue is the optimal timing for a husband to pronounce talaq sunnah within the wife's tuhr (pure period after menstruation).
The talaq sunnah requires the divorce to be pronounced in a tuhr during which no intercourse has occurred.
2
Examine the first view
Some mashāyikh hold that it is better to divorce at the end of the tuhr, just before the next menstruation. This shortens the iddah because the current tuhr does not count fully.
Reason: to avoid prolongation of the waiting period (tatwīl al-‘iddah).
3
Examine the second view (azhar)
Other mashāyikh, whose view the author calls 'azhar', hold that divorce should be pronounced immediately upon purification. Delaying increases the risk of intercourse, which would then violate the sunnah.
Reason: to prevent the husband from having intercourse after intending divorce, which would make the divorce against sunnah.
4
Analyze the reasoning
Both arguments are based on different objectives: one aims to reduce the woman's hardship (shorter iddah), the other aims to avoid a sunnah violation (intercourse within the same tuhr).
The first view sees no harm in delaying if it benefits the wife; the second sees a greater harm in potential sunnah violation.
5
Determine the tarjih
The author of al-Hidayah, al-Marghinani, declares the second view as 'azhar' (more apparent), indicating his preference. This is the relied-upon view in the Hanafi school.
Thus, the mufta bihi position is to pronounce divorce at the beginning of the tuhr.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
طلاق سنی میں مشائخ کا اختلاف ہے کہ اول طہر میں طلاق دینا اولی ہے یا آخر طہر میں۔ بعض کی رائے یہ ہے کہ آخر طہر میں طلاق دینا اولیٰ ہے۔ کیونکہ اس صورت میں عورت تطویل عدت سے بچ جائے گی۔ بایں طور کہ اگر ابتدائے طہر میں طلاق واقع کی تو عورت کی عدت تین طہر اور تین حیض ہو جائیں گے۔ اور اگر آخر طہر میں طلاق واقع کی تو اس عورت کی عدت دو طہر اور تین حیض ہوں گے ۔ ظاہر ہے کہ پہلی صورت میں تطویل عدت ہے اور دوسری میں تطویل عدت نہیں ہے اور بعض مشائخ کی رائے جس کو صاحب ہدایہ نے اظہر کہا ہے یہ ہے کہ جوں ہی عورت حیض سے پاک ہوئی اس کو طلاق دے دے۔ کیونکہ اگر اس کی طلاق کو مؤخر کیا گیا تو ممکن ہے کہ اس سے جماع کر بیٹھے اسلئے کہ یہ رغبت کا زمانہ ہے۔ اور حال یہ ہے کہ شوہر نے اس کو طلاق دینے کا ارادہ کر رکھا ہے۔ تو ایسی صورت میں یہ ایقاع طلاق جماع کے بعد ہو گا۔ اور ایسے طہر میں طلاق دینا جس میں جماع کیا گیا ہے سنت کے خلاف ہے اسلئے زیادہ بہتر یہی ہے کہ اول طہر میں طلاق دے دی جائے۔ واللہ اعلم !
There is a difference among the mashāyikh regarding the talaq sunnah: whether it is better to give the divorce at the beginning of the pure period or at the end. Some are of the opinion that it is better to give the divorce at the end of the pure period, because in that case the woman will avoid prolongation of the waiting period. That is, if he pronounces divorce at the beginning of the pure period, the woman's waiting period becomes three pure periods and three menstruations. If he pronounces divorce at the end of the pure period, her waiting period becomes two pure periods and three menstruations. Obviously, in the first case there is prolongation of waiting period; in the second there is no prolongation. Some other mashāyikh, whose view the author of al-Hidayah called azhar (more apparent), are of the opinion that as soon as the woman becomes pure from menstruation, he should give her the divorce, because if the divorce is delayed, it is possible that he may have intercourse with her, as this is a time of desire, whereas he intends to divorce. In such a case, the pronouncement of divorce will occur after intercourse. To give divorce in a pure period during which intercourse has taken place is against the sunnah. Therefore, it is better to give the divorce at the beginning of the pure period. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf (difference of opinion) regarding the optimal timing of pronouncing talaq sunnah within the purity period (tuhr). The dispute is among the mashāyikh of the Hanafi school. One group argues that delaying the divorce to the end of the tuhr is better (awla) because it shortens the woman's waiting period. They reason: if a divorce is given at the beginning of a tuhr, the waiting period consists of three full tuhrs plus three periods of menstruation, because the current tuhr counts as one, and she must complete three more menstrual cycles. But if divorce is given at the very end, just before menstruation begins, the current tuhr does not count fully, resulting in only two more tuhrs and three menstruations, thus avoiding prolongation. The other group, whose view is described as azhar (more apparent) by the author of al-Hidayah (al-Marghinani), holds that the divorce should be pronounced immediately upon purification. Their reason: delaying may lead the husband to have intercourse with his wife during this legally permissible time of desire, which would then require him to pronounce divorce after intercourse – a practice that is against the sunnah (since the ideal is to pronounce divorce in a tuhr without intercourse). Hence, immediate pronouncement is safer and more in line with the sunnah. The author concludes with 'Wallahu a‘lam' (And Allah knows best), indicating this is the preferred view.

Key Terms
تطویل عدت (tatwīl al-‘iddah): Prolongation of the waiting period (iddah) for the divorced woman.
اظہر (azhar): Meaning 'more apparent' or 'stronger', used by the author of al-Hidayah to indicate the preferred view among the Hanafi scholars.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the view called 'azhar' by the author of al-Hidayah, when is it better to give divorce during the wife's purity period?
A) At the end, to shorten the waiting period.
B) Immediately at the beginning, to avoid intercourse after intention.
C) At any time, as long as it's in a tuhr without intercourse.
D) It is better not to divorce if the couple might reconcile.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has a valid internal dispute on the optimal timing of talaq sunnah, but the azhar view, which recommends immediate divorce upon purification, is the preferred position.

Talaq Bid'ah and the Shafi'i Objection
Introducing talaq bid'ah and beginning the Shafi'i objection on permissibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of talaq bid'ah, explain why it is considered sinful yet legally effective, and identify the beginning of the Shafi'i argument that all divorces are permissible.

Core Idea
Talaq bid'ah is sinful but valid; the Shafi'i school argues it is entirely permissible.

In this lesson, we examine talaq bid'ah — a divorce that violates the prophetic sunnah. The Hanafi school rules that such a divorce takes effect but the husband commits a sin. Imam al-Shafi'i, however, maintains that any form of divorce is permissible because it is a legally valid act. The passage you are about to read presents both positions, though the Shafi'i argument is cut short. We will unpack what is available and understand the core of the disagreement.

Guided Path
1
Define talaq bid'ah
Identify the precise definition given in the text: pronouncing three divorces in one utterance or three in a single purity period.
This definition is the basis for the dispute.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
The Hanafi position: the divorce occurs (waqa'a al-talāq) and the husband is sinful (kāna 'āṣiyan). Understand the dual consequence: legal effect but moral sin.
Sinfulness does not nullify the divorce.
3
Identify the Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that every divorce is permissible (mubāḥ) because it is a legally sanctioned disposal (taṣarruf mashrū') from which the ruling is derived (yustafādu bihi al-ḥukm).
The text cuts off; the full argument likely continues that legality and sin cannot coexist.
4
Analyse the basis of disagreement
The dispute hinges on whether the manner of pronouncing divorce can render an otherwise valid act sinful. Hanafis separate the act's validity from its conformity to sunnah; Shafi'is appear to argue that any valid act cannot be sinful.
This is a methodological difference in how they view the relationship between legal validity and moral permissibility.

Commentary
This passage, though truncated, introduces talaq bid'ah (innovated divorce) and presents Imam al-Shafi'i's view that all divorces are permissible (mubah). The definition of talaq bid'ah is given: pronouncing three divorces in one utterance or three in a single purity period. The Hanafi position (implicit, as stated in the first part) is that such divorces take effect but are sinful (''asī). Al-Shafi'i's argument is that since divorce is a legally valid action, it cannot be sinful; any form of divorce is permissible as long as it accomplishes the legal effect. The passage cuts off with the Arabic word 'lā tajāmi' (are not compatible), likely arguing that sin and legal efficacy cannot coexist. Unfortunately, the Hanafi rebuttal is not present in this page, leaving the dispute incomplete.

Key Terms
طلاق بدعة (talāq bid‘ah): A divorce that does not follow the sunnah, such as giving three divorces in one utterance or three in one purity period.
بدعة (bid‘ah): Innovation in religious practice. Here it specifically refers to divorces that depart from the prophetic sunnah.
