Talaq — Divorce
advanced
8 min
The Ruling on Bid'ah Talaq and the Dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i
Explains bid'ah talaq and refutes Shafi'i's view

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that bid'ah talaq is haram but valid, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument regarding legitimacy.

Core Idea
A divorce can be sinful yet legally effective – prohibition does not negate occurrence.

When a husband gives three divorces in one utterance or in a single tuhr period, is the divorce valid? The Hanafi school teaches that such a divorce – called bid'ah (innovated) – is sinful (haram) but nevertheless takes effect, making the woman irrevocably separated. Imam al-Shafi'i disagreed, arguing that any legitimate action (tasarruf mashru') cannot be prohibited. This lesson unpacks the evidence from the hadith of Ibn Umar and the rational proofs, showing how the Hanafi school maintains the coexistence of sin and legal effectiveness.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi Position
Identify the exact ruling on bid'ah talaq: giving three divorces in one word or three in one tuhr. The Hanafi school says it is haram (sinful) but the divorces occur and the woman becomes bain (irrevocably separate).
Bid'ah talaq is not invalid; it is valid but sinful.
2
Identify the Opponent and Their View
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that every divorce is permissible (mubah). He argues that divorce is a legitimate action (tasarruf mashru') because it produces legal effects (occurrence of divorce), and legitimacy cannot coexist with prohibition.
Shafi'i's position: no divorce is sinful; all forms are equally permissible.
3
Follow the Opponent's Proof
Examine Shafi'i's dalil: Since divorce brings about the legal consequence of separation, it is mashru' and thus cannot be haram. The only prohibited aspect in divorce during menstruation is the prolongation of iddah, not the divorce itself.
Shafi'i distinguishes between the act and its timing.
4
Analyse the Hanafi Response
The Hanafi response: (1) The original rule (asl) in divorce is prohibition because it cuts off marriage – a bond with religious and worldly benefits. (2) Permissibility is granted only by necessity (hajah) for release. (3) Combining three divorces has no necessity; the need is met by one divorce in each tuhr. (4) Legality and prohibition can coexist, as seen in divorce during menstruation – prohibited yet effective. This refutes Shafi'i's premise.
The hadith of Ibn Umar explicitly says giving three divorces together is a sin but bainunah occurs.
5
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf
The practical consequence: According to Shafi'i, giving three divorces in one utterance is permissible and not sinful; the wife becomes bain but the husband has not committed a sin. According to Hanafis, the same act is a major sin (haram), yet the divorce is valid and the wife is bain. The ruling on sinfulness affects the husband's moral and legal accountability (e.g., need for tawbah, potential ta'zir).
Both schools agree on the legal effect (divorce occurs), but differ on the moral classification and permissibility.

اور دنیوی
ترجمہ اور طلاق بدعت یہ ہے کہ (مرد) اس کو ایک کلمہ سے تین طلاق دے یا ایک طہر میں تین ( طلاق دے ) پس جب یہ کر لیا تو طلاق واقع ہوگئی اور (وہ) گنہ گار ہے۔ اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ ہر طلاق مباح ہے۔ کیونکہ وہ تصرف مشروع ہے حتی کہ طلاق سے حکم مستفاد ہوتا ہے۔ اور مشروعیت ممانعت کے ساتھ جمع نہیں ہوسکتی۔ بخلاف حالت حیض میں طلاق کے، کیونکہ محرم اس پر عدت کو طول دینا ہے نہ کہ طلاق ۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ طلاق میں اصل ممانعت ہے کیونکہ طلاق میں اس نکاح کو قطع کرنا ہے جس کے ساتھ دینی مصلحتیں متعلق ہیں۔ اور اباحت چھٹکارا پانے کی ضرورت کی وجہ سے ہے۔ اور تین کو جمع کرنے کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں ۔ اور حاجت ان طہروں پر متفرق کرنے میں ثابت ہے دلیل حاجت کی طرف نظر کرتے ہوئے ۔ اور حاجت بذات خود باقی ہے۔ لہذا دلیل کو حاجت پر تصور کرنا ممکن ہے اور (طلاق بدعی کا) مشروع ہونا اس حیثیت سے کہ وہ رقیت کا ازالہ ہے منافی نہیں ممانعت کے ایسے معنی کی وجہ سے جو اس کے غیر میں ہے۔ اور وہ معنیٰ وہ ہے جو ہم نے ذکر کیا۔ اور ایسے ہی دو ( طلاق) کا واقع کرنا ایک طہر میں بدعت ہے۔ اسکی وجہ سے جو ہم نے کہا اور ایک بائنہ میں روایت مختلف ہوگئی۔ امام محمد نے مبسوط میں کہا کہ یہ سنت سے تجاوز ہے۔ اسلئے کہ چھٹکارا پانے میں صفت زائدہ ثابت کرنے کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ اور وہ بینونت ہے۔ اور زیادات کی روایت میں مکروہ نہیں فوری چھٹکارا پانے کی ضرورت کی وجہ ہے۔
تشریح طلاق بدعت یہ ہے کہ شوہر اپنی منکوحہ کو ایک کلمہ سے تین طلاق دے۔ یا ایک طہر میں تین طلاق واقع کرے۔ یہ ہمارے نزدیک حرام ہے لیکن اگر ایسا کر دیا تو طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی۔ اور عورت کیلئے حرمت غلیظہ ثابت ہوگی اور طلاق دینے والا کہنہ گار ہوگا۔ امام شافعی کا مذ ہب یہ ہے کہ ہر طلاق مباح ہے۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل ہ یہ ہے کہ طلاق تصرف مشروع ہے۔ چنانچہ طلاق سے حکم طلاق مستفاد ہوتا ہے۔ اور حکم طلاق ، وقوع طلاق ہے۔ حاصل یہ کہ طلاق پر اثر شرعی یعنی وقوع طلاق مرتب ہوتا ہے اور جس چیز پر اثر شرعی مرتب ہو جائے وہ امر مشروع کہلائے گا۔ لہذا طلاق امر مشروع ہوئی اور جو چیز مشروع ہے وہ ممنوع نہیں ہو سکتی کیونکہ مشروعیت ممانعت کے ساتھ جمع نہیں ہو سکتی ہے۔ بخلاف الطلاق سے اعتراض کا جواب ہے۔ اعتراض یہ ہے کہ امام شافعی کا یہ کہنا کہ مشروعیت ممانعت کے ساتھ جمع نہیں ہوسکتی غلط ہے۔ اسلئے کہ حالت حیض میں طلاق دینا حرام ہے۔ حالانکہ اس پر حکم شرعی یعنی وقوع طلاق مرتب ہوتا ہے۔ پس اس صورت میں مشروعیت اور ممانعت دونوں جمع ہو گئے ہیں۔ امام شافعی کی طرف سے جواب یہ ہو گا کہ حالت حیض میں نفس طلاق حرام نہیں بلکہ عورت پر
Ashraf al-Hidayah, Urdu commentary of Hidayah, Volume Four. Book of Divorce. That this is bid'ah divorce, and only one divorce is permissible. Imam Malik's evidence is that prohibition is the original rule in divorce, due to the Prophet's saying, 'Marry and do not divorce' (narrated by Abu Dawud), meaning marry and do not divorce. Permissibility of divorce is due to the need to get rid of the wife. And the need is fulfilled by one divorce; therefore a second divorce would not be permissible. Our evidence is the hadith of Ibn Umar. Summary of the hadith: Abdullah ibn Umar divorced his wife during menstruation. Then he intended to give two more divorces in two tuhr periods. The Prophet was informed of this and said, 'O Ibn Umar, Allah did not command you to do this; you have missed the sunnah. The sunnah is that you wait for the tuhr, then give divorce in each tuhr.' Then he commanded me, so I took her back. Then he said, 'When she becomes pure, then divorce her at that time or keep her.' I said, 'O Messenger of Allah, if I give her three divorces, will it be lawful for me to take her back?' He said, 'No, she becomes bain (irrevocably separated) and it is a sin.' This hadith is narrated by Dar Qutni. From this hadith it is understood that giving three divorces separately in three tuhr periods is sunnah. The rational evidence is that the need for divorce is an internal matter; it is impossible to be aware of it. Therefore the ruling is based on its evidence. The evidence of the need for divorce is the action of giving divorce in a tuhr period. Whenever the evidence of need is repeated, the need for divorce is repeated. When the need for divorce is repeated, then repetition of divorce is also permissible. Therefore our view is that giving three divorces separately in three tuhr periods is permissible, not bid'ah. There is a difference of opinion among the mashayikh regarding talaq sunni: whether it is better to give divorce at the beginning of the tuhr or at the end. Some are of the opinion that giving divorce at the end of the tuhr is better, because in that case the woman will avoid prolongation of iddah. If divorce is given at the beginning of the tuhr, the woman's iddah will be three tuhrs and three menstruations. If divorce is given at the end of the tuhr, her iddah will be two tuhrs and three menstruations. Obviously, in the first case there is prolongation of iddah, in the second there is not. Some mashayikh, whom Sahib al-Hidayah called azhar (most apparent), are of the opinion that as soon as the woman becomes pure from menstruation, he should give her divorce, because if the divorce is delayed, it is possible that he may have intercourse with her, as this is a time of desire, and he has already intended to divorce her. In such a case, the divorce would occur after intercourse, and giving divorce in a tuhr in which intercourse has taken place is against the sunnah; therefore it is better to give divorce at the beginning of the tuhr. And Allah knows best! Bid'ah divorce... Imam Shafi'i's viewpoint. And bid'ah divorce is that he gives her three divorces with one word or three in one tuhr; if he does so, divorce occurs and he is sinful. Al-Shafi'i said that every divorce is permissible because it is a legitimate action, so that the ruling is derived from it, and legitimacy does not coexist with prohibition. Unlike divorce during menstruation, because the prohibited thing is prolongation of iddah, not the divorce itself. Our evidence is that the original rule in divorce is prohibition because it involves cutting off marriage, to which religious and worldly interests are attached. Permissibility is due to the need for release, and there is no need to combine three [divorces]. The need is established for [giving them] separately over tuhr periods, considering its evidence. The need itself remains; therefore it is possible to conceive evidence for it. Its being legitimate in itself, as removal of bondage, does not contradict prohibition due to a meaning in something else, which we have mentioned. Similarly, giving two divorces in one tuhr is bid'ah due to what we have said. There is a difference of narration regarding one bain divorce. In al-Asl, it is said that he has erred from the sunnah because there is no need to establish an additional quality in release, namely bainunah. In Riwayat al-Ziyadat, it is not disliked due to the need for immediate release.
Source pages p. 224

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah deals with the ruling on bid'ah divorce and the difference between the Hanafi school and Imam Shafi'i. It begins by stating that bid'ah divorce (giving three divorces in one utterance or in one tuhr period) is sinful but effective. The author first refutes Imam Malik's position that only one divorce is permissible, by citing the hadith of Ibn Umar, which proves that the sunnah is to give one divorce in each tuhr (three separate tuhrs). The hadith also shows that giving three divorces together is sinful but they take effect. The author then presents the rational argument: the need for divorce is internal, and its evidence is the act of giving divorce in a tuhr. If the need is repeated (as evidenced by repeated actions), then multiple divorces are permissible. Next, there is a discussion among Hanafi scholars about the best time to give sunni divorce: at the beginning or end of the tuhr. The view preferred by Sahib al-Hidayah is to give it immediately upon purity to avoid intercourse that would break the sunnah. Then the text addresses Imam Shafi'i's view that all divorces are permissible (mubah). Shafi'i argues that divorce is a legitimate action because it produces legal effects (occurrence of divorce), and legitimacy cannot coexist with prohibition. The Hanafi response is that the original rule of divorce is prohibition (hazr) due to cutting off marriage, and permissibility is only due to necessity (hajah). Since there is no necessity to combine three divorces, that form remains prohibited. Furthermore, Shafi'i's principle is refuted by the example of divorce during menstruation, which is prohibited yet legally effective—showing that permissibility and prohibition can coexist in terms of the act's validity and its ruling. The passage also notes a difference of narration within the Hanafi school about giving a single bain (irrevocable) divorce: according to al-Asl (Imam Muhammad) it is an error; according to Riwayat al-Ziyadat, it is not disliked if there is a need for immediate release.

Key Terms
طلاق بدعت (talaq al-bid'ah): Divorce that is sinful but effective: giving three divorces in one utterance or three in one tuhr period.
طلاق سنی (talaq al-sunnah): The correct sunnah divorce: one divorce in each tuhr without intercourse, allowing revocation during iddah.
حاجت (hajah): Need or necessity that makes an otherwise prohibited action permissible; here, the need to end marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school in this passage, what is the ruling on giving three divorces in one utterance?
A) It is permissible and valid.
B) It is sinful but the divorces take effect.
C) It is invalid and no divorce occurs.
D) It is only makruh tanzihi.

Key Takeaway
Bid'ah divorce is haram but valid; the Shafi'i view that all divorces are permissible is rejected based on hadith and rational proof.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
10 min
Bid'ah Divorce and the Hanafi-Shafi'i Dispute
Explains bid'ah divorce, Hanafi position, and responds to Shafi'i objections

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on bid'ah divorce, explain the Hanafi proof based on original prohibition and necessity (hajah), and respond to the Shafi'i objection that prescription and prohibition cannot coexist.

Core Idea
Bid'ah divorce is valid but sinful: the original ruling on divorce is prohibition, and permissibility is only for necessity.

Divorce is a serious matter that severs a marriage bond, which carries many religious and worldly benefits. Both the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools agree that certain forms of divorce are valid, but they differ on whether a 'bid'ah' (innovative) form—such as giving three divorces in one utterance—is permissible or sinful. In this lesson, we will examine the core arguments of each school, focusing on the Hanafi use of the principle that the original ruling on divorce is prohibition, and that permissibility is granted only to the extent of genuine need (hajah).

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on bid'ah divorce
Identify what qualifies as bid'ah divorce (three divorces in one utterance or in one period of purity) and state the ruling: it is haram (sinful) but the divorce is effective (waqi').
The sin is due to violating the proper method, not because the divorce is invalid.
2
Identify the Shafi'i position and its proof
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that every divorce is mubah (permissible) because divorce is a prescribed action (tasarruf mashru')—a legal effect (occurrence) is attached to it. In his usul, prescription cannot coexist with prohibition.
The Shafi'i proof relies on the concept that anything with a legal effect must be legislated, hence permissible.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i proof
The Hanafis argue that prescription and prohibition can coexist, as seen in divorce during menstruation. They then present their own proof: the original ruling on divorce is prohibition (hazr) because it severs marriage with its attendant religious and worldly benefits. Permissibility is only due to necessity (hajah). Since there is no necessity to combine three divorces, doing so remains forbidden.
The Hanafi response includes a rebuttal to the Shafi'i analogy with menstrual divorce.
4
Examine the role of hajah (need) in the Hanafi argument
The key to the Hanafi position is that permissibility is granted only to the extent of need. The need for release from a marriage is satisfied with one divorce; combining three is unnecessary. However, separate divorces over three tuhrs are permitted because the need continues (e.g., to close the door to return if the wife is ill-tempered).
This explains why separate triple divorce is sunnah, not bid'ah.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The practical difference: Hanafis consider triple divorce in one sitting valid but sinful; the wife becomes irrevocably prohibited (hurmah ghalizah) and the husband commits a sin. Shafi'is consider it valid and permissible (or at most makruh), with no sin.
Both schools affirm validity, but the ethical ruling differs.

والحاجة في نفسها باقية سے بھی اشکال کا جواب ہے۔ اشکال یہ ہے کہ دلیل حاجت ، حاجت کے قائم مقام اس صورت میں ہو گی جبکہ حاجت کا وجود متصور ہو اور یہاں حاجت کا وجود متصور نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ جب طہر اول میں ایک طلاق واقع کر دی گئی اور اس کی وجہ سے نکاح مرتفع ہو گیا تو اب نکاح کی ذمہ داری سے چھٹکارا پانے کی کیا حاجت رہ گئی۔ اور جب حاجت طلاق نہ رہی تو دلیل حاجت بھی اس کے قائم مقام نہ ہوگی۔
جواب ... حاجت طلاق بذات خود باقی ہے لہذا دلیل کو حاجت پر تصور کرنا ممکن ہے۔ حاجت طلاق کے باقی رہنے کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ بسا اوقات عورت بد اخلاق اور بد زبان ہوتی ہے اور مرد جعت یا تجدید نکاح کے ذریعہ تدارک کے امکان کے دروازہ کو بند کرنا چاہتا ہے۔ اس حاجت کی وجہ سے شریعت نے اس کو دوسرے اور تیسرے طہر میں ایک ایک طلاق دینے کی اجازت دے دی تا کہ عورت کیلئے حرمت غلیظہ ثابت ہو جائے اور ندامت کے وقت تدارک کا امکان باقی نہ رہے۔
And bid'ah divorce is that a man gives three divorces in one utterance or three divorces in one period of purity. When he does this, divorce occurs and he is sinful. Imam al-Shafi'i said that every divorce is permissible, because it is a prescribed action, so much so that a ruling is derived from divorce. And permissibility cannot coexist with prohibition. Unlike divorce during menstruation, because the prohibited matter is prolonging the waiting period, not the divorce itself. Our proof is that the original ruling on divorce is prohibition, because divorce cuts the marriage which has religious and worldly interests attached to it. Permissibility is due to the need for release. There is no need to combine three, and the need is established in separating them over periods of purity, considering the evidence of need. And the need itself remains. So it is possible to conceive the evidence upon the need. And the prescribed nature of bid'ah divorce, in that it is a removal of the marriage bond, does not contradict prohibition due to a meaning in something else, which we have mentioned. Similarly, divorcing twice in one period of purity is bid'ah for the same reason. And the narration differs regarding the single irrevocable divorce. Imam Muhammad said in al-Mabsut that it is against the Sunnah, because there is no need to prove an additional quality in release, which is irrevocability. And in the narration of al-Ziyadat, it is not disliked due to the need for immediate release.
Explanation: Bid'ah divorce is that a husband gives his wife three divorces in one utterance, or gives three divorces in one period of purity. According to us, this is forbidden, but if he does it, divorce occurs and severe prohibition (hurmah ghalizah) is established for the woman, and the one giving divorce is sinful. Imam al-Shafi'i's school is that every divorce is permissible. Imam al-Shafi'i's proof is that divorce is a prescribed action. So a ruling of divorce is derived from divorce. And the ruling of divorce is its occurrence. In summary, a legal effect, i.e., occurrence of divorce, is attached to divorce. And anything to which a legal effect is attached is called a prescribed matter. Therefore divorce becomes a prescribed matter. And a prescribed matter cannot be prohibited because prescription cannot coexist with prohibition. This is a response to the objection from divorce in menstruation. The objection is that Imam al-Shafi'i's statement that prescription cannot coexist with prohibition is wrong, because giving divorce during menstruation is forbidden, yet a legal ruling i.e., occurrence of divorce is attached to it. So in this case, both prescription and prohibition coexist. The response from Imam al-Shafi'i would be that in the case of menstruation, the divorce itself is not forbidden; rather, prolonging the waiting period for the woman is forbidden. Because when he divorces during menstruation, that menstrual period with intercourse will not count in the waiting period. Similarly, if he divorces in a period of purity in which he had intercourse with the woman, then in that period the divorce itself is not forbidden; rather, the forbidden matter is the confusion regarding the waiting period. Because we do not know whether she is pregnant so that the waiting period ends with delivery, or not pregnant so that according to us it ends with menstruation and according to the Shafi'is with periods of purity. After this response, no objection will remain against the Shafi'is.
Our proof is that the original ruling on divorce is prohibition, because divorce cuts the marriage which has religious and worldly interests attached. Religious interests: through marriage, the private part is protected from fornication which is forbidden in all religions. Worldly interests: after marriage, the woman gets maintenance and housing, and the man acquires offspring, etc. Whatever causes loss of religious and worldly interests should not be permitted in shari'ah. So reason demands that divorce be absolutely impermissible, but we made it permissible due to the need for release from the wife. And there is no need to combine three divorces, because the objective is achieved with less. For this reason, combining three divorces is forbidden in our school. 'And it is in separation over the periods of purity' addresses a question. The question is: just as there is no need to combine three divorces, similarly there is no need to give three divorces separately over three periods of purity, so this should also be forbidden, yet the Hanafis call this sunnah divorce. The answer is that the need for giving three divorces separately over three periods of purity is established, considering the evidence of need. And that evidence is action upon divorce at the time of intense aversion. 'And the need in itself remains' addresses another difficulty. The difficulty is that evidence of need takes the place of need only when the existence of need is conceivable. Here, the existence of need is not conceivable because when the first divorce was given in the first period of purity, and the marriage was dissolved due to it, what need remains for release from marital obligations? And when the need for divorce no longer exists, then the evidence of need also will not take its place. Answer: The need for divorce itself remains. So it is possible to conceive the evidence upon the need. The reason the need for divorce remains is that sometimes the woman is ill-tempered and foul-mouthed, and the man wants to close the door of rectification through return or renewal of marriage. Due to this need, the shari'ah allowed him to give one divorce in the second and third periods of purity, so that severe prohibition (hurmah ghalizah) is established for the woman and the possibility of rectification is removed at the time of regret.
Source pages p. 225

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafis and Imam al-Shafi'i (and his school) regarding the ruling of bid'ah divorce (giving three divorces in one utterance or in one tuhr). The author begins by defining bid'ah divorce and stating the Hanafi position: it is sinful (haram) but effective (waqi'). Then he presents Imam al-Shafi'i's view that every divorce is permissible (mubah). The Shafi'i proof is that divorce is a prescribed action (tasarruf mashru') because a legal effect (occurrence of divorce) is attached to it; anything with a legal effect is prescribed, and prescription cannot coexist with prohibition. The Shafi'i school also distinguishes divorce during menstruation: they say it is not the divorce itself that is forbidden, but the prolongation of the 'iddah. The Hanafi response is that the original ruling on divorce is prohibition because it severs marital bonds that carry religious and worldly benefits (masalih). Permissibility is granted only due to necessity (hajah) for release from a bad marriage. There is no necessity to combine three divorces at once; the need is fulfilled by separating them over three tuhrs. The Hanafis also address the objection that if there is no need for combined triple divorce, why is there a need for separate triple divorce? They answer that the need for separate triple divorce is established by evidence of need (dalil al-hajah), i.e., the prophetic practice of allowing divorce at times of aversion. Another objection concerns the continuation of need after the first divorce: the marriage ends, so why give two more? The author responds that the need remains because sometimes the man wants to make the woman irrevocably prohibited (hurmah ghalizah) to prevent any possibility of return, especially if she is ill-tempered. This rationale allows the second and third divorces in separate tuhrs, making it sunnah divorce. There is also an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf regarding a single irrevocable divorce (al-wahidah al-ba'inah). According to Imam Muhammad in al-Mabsut, it is against the Sunnah because there is no need for the additional effect of irrevocability; but according to a narration in al-Ziyadat, it is not disliked due to the need for immediate release.

Key Terms
طلاق بدعت (talaq bid'ah): A divorce that is innovative, such as giving three divorces in one utterance or in one period of purity.
حاجت (hajah): Need or necessity that makes something permissible despite the original prohibition.
مشروعیت (mashru'iyyah): The quality of being prescribed or legal in shari'ah; having a legal effect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on a husband giving his wife three divorces in one utterance?
A) The divorce is invalid and does not occur.
B) The divorce occurs and the husband is not sinful.
C) The divorce occurs and the husband is sinful.
D) The divorce is invalid unless the husband intended three separate divorces.

Key Takeaway
Bid'ah divorce (triple in one sitting) is valid but sinful in the Hanafi school; the original prohibition on divorce is overridden only by necessity, and combining three is unnecessary.

Three Divorces in One Sitting: Hanafi Prohibition and Refutation of Shafi'i Proof
Inter-madhhab dispute with proof and refutation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on three divorces in one sitting and refute the Shafi'i argument that legislation cannot coexist with prohibition, using the Hanafi distinction between prohibition li-dhatihi and li-ghayrihi.

Core Idea
Three divorces in one sitting are haram because necessity does not require them; the Shafi'i claim fails for prohibition li-ghayrihi.

This passage tackles a key inter-madhhab dispute: whether a man who pronounces three divorces in one sitting commits a prohibited act. The Hanafi school rules it haram, while the Shafi'i school considers it valid and permissible. The Hanafi proof rests on the original prohibition of divorce due to loss of marital interests, permitted only to the extent of need. The passage also refutes the Shafi'i objection that legislation cannot coexist with prohibition, by distinguishing prohibition in itself from prohibition for another reason, using the classic example of prayer on usurped land.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the Hanafi ruling on three divorces in one sitting and the reasoning behind it.
The Hanafi position is that it is haram but legally effective.
2
Identify the Shafi'i view and their proof
What does the Shafi'i school hold, and what is their key argument from usul al-fiqh?
They argue that since divorce is legislated, it cannot be prohibited.
3
Follow the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i proof
The Hanafi response uses a distinction in the type of prohibition. How does the prayer-on-usurped-land analogy illustrate it?
Prohibition li-ghayrihi can coexist with legislation.
4
Analyse the Hanafi's own positive proof
Examine the Quranic and logical grounds: original prohibition of divorce, necessity for separation, and the Quranic phrase 'Divorce is twice'.
The verse implies separation over multiple occasions, not all at once.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical difference between the two schools in terms of the ruling on the act and its legal effects?
Both agree the divorces count, but differ on sinfulness.

Prolonging the 'iddah is forbidden. Because when divorce is given during menstruation, this menstruation after intercourse is not counted in the 'iddah. Similarly, if divorce is given in a tuhr in which he has had intercourse with the woman, then in that tuhr the divorce itself is not forbidden, but the matter of 'iddah becomes ambiguous. Because we do not know whether she is pregnant so that she completes 'iddah with childbirth, or not pregnant so that according to us she completes 'iddah with menstruations and according to Shafi'is with tuhrs. After this answer, no objection will remain against the Shafi'is. Our proof is that the original ruling on divorce is prohibition. Because due to divorce, the marriage is severed, with which religious and worldly interests are connected. Religious interests are that through marriage the private parts are protected from zina, which is forbidden in all religions, and worldly interests are that after marriage the wife gets nafaqah and the husband gets the acquisition of offspring, etc. And something through which religious and worldly interests are lost should not be permissible in the Shari'ah. Therefore, reason requires that divorce be absolutely impermissible, but we have made divorce permissible due to the need to be free from the wife. And there is no need to combine three divorces, because the purpose is achieved with less than three. For this reason, according to us, combining three divorces is forbidden. 'And it is in separation over tuhrs' is an answer to a question. The question is: Just as there is no need to combine three divorces, similarly there is no need to give three divorces separately over three tuhrs, so it should also be forbidden, whereas the Hanafis call it sunnah divorce. The summary of the answer is that the need is established for giving three divorces separately over three tuhrs. Looking at the proof of need, and that proof is proceeding with divorce at a time when desire is renewed. 'And the need in itself remains' is also an answer to an objection. The objection is that the proof of need will stand in place of need only if the existence of need is conceivable, and here the existence of need is not conceivable. Because when the first divorce is given in the first tuhr and the marriage is terminated due to it, what need remains to be free from the responsibility of marriage? And when the need for divorce remains no longer, the proof of need will also not stand in its place. The answer: The need for divorce remains in itself, so it is possible to conceive the proof upon the need. The reason for the need for divorce remaining is that sometimes the woman is ill-tempered and foul-mouthed, and the man wants to close the door of rectification through raj'ah or renewal of marriage for the second and third divorces. Due to this need, the Shari'ah has permitted him to give one divorce each in the second and third tuhrs so that severe prohibition (hurmah ghalizah) is established for the woman and the possibility of rectification remains no more at the time of regret. But then there is an objection that this proof requires that three divorces with one expression should be permissible, whereas you say it is prohibited. Its answer is that the proof conflicts with the text. By 'text' is meant the hadith of Ibn Umar or the verse 'Divorce is twice' which indicates separate divorces, and it is obvious that proof is not given precedence over text. As for the Shafi'i proof that 'legislation does not coexist with prohibition', its answer is that something legislated in itself cannot coexist with something prohibited in itself, but something legislated in itself can coexist with something prohibited for another reason. Like performing prayer on usurped land and selling at the time of Friday azan: the prayer itself and the sale itself are legislated, but they become prohibited for another reason (due to usurped land and abandoning the effort for Friday). Similarly, in the mentioned issue, divorce itself is legislated, and it is prohibited for another reason due to the loss of marital interests.
Source pages p. 226

Commentary
This passage discusses the prohibition of giving three divorces in one sitting and the Hanafi refutation of the Shafi'i argument. The author first explains that prolonging 'iddah is forbidden if divorce is given during menstruation or in a tuhr after intercourse because the 'iddah becomes ambiguous. The Hanafi proof is that divorce is originally prohibited due to the loss of religious and worldly interests of marriage, but necessity makes it permissible. Since there is no need for three divorces at once, combining them is haram. The passage then answers two objections: (1) why separative divorces over three tuhrs are allowed (due to remaining need), and (2) why the proof of need does not justify three in one expression (because it conflicts with the Quranic text 'Divorce is twice'). Finally, it refutes the Shafi'i proof that 'legislation does not coexist with prohibition' by distinguishing between prohibition in itself and prohibition for another reason, giving examples like prayer on usurped land.

Key Terms
مشروع لذاتہ (mashru' li-dhatihi): Something that is legislated in its own right, having intrinsic permissibility.
ممنوع لغیرہ (mamnu' li-ghayrihi): Something that is prohibited not because of its own nature but due to an external factor.
حاجت (hajah): Necessity that makes a normally prohibited act permissible, but only to the extent needed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Three divorces in one sentence are haram in the Hanafi school because they combine multiple divorces without necessity, but they are nonetheless legally effective.

Talaq — Divorce

Two Divorces in One Tuhr: The Ruling of Bid'ah
Ruling on two divorces in one tuhr being bid'ah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on giving two divorces in one tuhr and explain why it is considered bid'ah.

Core Idea
Two divorces in one tuhr is bid'ah (makruh tahrimi) because there is no need to combine them.

In this lesson, we examine a specific scenario in talaq: a husband giving two divorces in a single tuhr (pure period). The Hanafi school rules this as bid'ah, meaning it is an innovation contrary to the sunnah. We will explore the reasoning behind this ruling and its legal effect.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Recognize that the act is giving two divorces in one tuhr. The ruling is that it is bid'ah (innovated) and makruh tahrimi (sinful).
The divorce itself is still effective; only the manner is sinful.
2
Understand the reason
The author states that the reason is that there is no need (hajat) to combine two divorces in one tuhr. The sunnah method is to give one divorce per tuhr.
This is based on the principle that necessity is measured by its extent.
3
Note the hukm level
The act is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked) due to being bid'ah. It is not haram, nor does it invalidate the divorce.
Makruh tahrimi is the level just below haram in Hanafi fiqh.
4
Recognize practical effect
Despite being sinful, both divorces count, and the marriage ends after the second divorce (if it is the third, it becomes irrevocable).
The husband should repent but the divorces are legally binding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ دو طلاق کا ایک طہر میں واقع کرنا بھی بدعت ہے۔ دلیل حاجت الی الجمع کی وجہ سے۔ اگر کسی نے اپنی بیوی کو ایک طلاق بائن ایسے طہر میں دی جس میں اسکے ساتھ جماع نہیں کیا گیا تو اس بارے میں ہمارے علماء سے روایات مختلف ہیں۔ چنانچہ امام محمد نے مبسوط میں فرمایا کہ یہ خلاف سنت ہے۔ اسلئے کہ عورت سے چھٹکارا پانے میں بینونت جو صفت زائدہ ہے اس کو ثابت کرنے کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ زیادات میں روایت یہ ہے کہ ایک طلاق بائنہ میں کوئی کراہت نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ بھی فوری چھٹکارے کی ضرورت پیش آجاتی ہے۔ اور فوری چھٹکارا صفت بینونت کے بغیر نہیں ہو سکتا۔ اسلئے اس صفت کو زیادہ کرنے میں کوئی کراہت نہیں۔
سوال .. صاحب ہدایہ کیلئے مناسب یہ تھا کہ فرماتے فی زیادات الزیادات اسلئے کہ امام محمد نے اس مسئلہ کو زیادات الزیادات میں ذکر کیا ہے نہ کہ زیادات میں۔ لیکن جواب میں کہا جا سکتا ہے کہ کاتب سے سہو ہو گیا۔ اور یہ بھی احتمال ہے کہ مصنف ہدایہ نے یہی کہا ہو۔ کیونکہ زیادات الزیادات، زیادات کا ہی تمہ ہے۔ پس زیادات الزیادات کا مسئلہ زیادات ہی کا مسئلہ شمار ہو گا ۔ ( عینی شرح ہدایہ ) فوائد طلاق سنت میں مذاہب کا حاصل یہ ہیکہ ہمارے نزدیک طلاق سنت میں تفریق اور وقت دونوں معتبر ہیں ۔ اور امام مالک کے نزدیک ایک طالق اور وقت معتبر ہے اور امام شافعی کے نزیک صرف وقت معتبر ہے عدد کا اعتبار نہیں ہے ۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب
The author of Al-Hidayah says that giving two divorces in one tuhr is also bid'ah, due to the proof of need for combining. If someone gives his wife one bain divorce in a tuhr in which he has not had intercourse with her, then in this regard there are different narrations from our scholars. Thus, Imam Muhammad said in al-Mabsut that this is against the Sunnah, because in getting rid of the wife, there is no need to establish the extra quality of baynunah. In al-Ziyadat, the narration is that there is no dislikedness in one bain divorce, because sometimes the need for immediate separation arises, and immediate separation cannot occur without the quality of baynunah. Therefore, there is no dislikedness in adding this quality. Question: It would have been appropriate for the author of Al-Hidayah to say 'in Ziyadat al-Ziyadat' because Imam Muhammad mentioned this issue in Ziyadat al-Ziyadat, not in al-Ziyadat. But in answer, it can be said that the scribe made an error. And it is also possible that the author of Al-Hidayah said this, because Ziyadat al-Ziyadat is itself a supplement to al-Ziyadat. So the issue from Ziyadat al-Ziyadat is considered part of al-Ziyadat. (Ayni Sharh al-Hidayah) The summary of the schools regarding sunnah divorce is that according to us, both separation and time are considered. According to Imam Malik, one divorce and time are considered. According to Imam Shafi'i, only time is considered, number is not considered. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 227

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on giving two divorces in one tuhr and the different Hanafi narrations on giving a single bain divorce in a tuhr without intercourse. The author states that two divorces in one tuhr are bid'ah because there is no need to combine them; the necessity is only for one divorce at a time. For a single bain divorce in a tuhr without intercourse, Imam Muhammad in al-Mabsut considers it against the Sunnah, but in al-Ziyadat, there is a narration that it is not disliked, as necessity may require immediate separation which only bain divorce provides. The author then addresses a textual issue: the Hidayah refers to 'al-Ziyadat' but the correct reference is 'Ziyadat al-Ziyadat', but this is deemed acceptable as the latter is part of the former. Finally, the author summarizes the positions of the schools on sunnah divorce: Hanafis require both separation over three tuhrs and timing (tuhr without intercourse); Malikis require one divorce and correct timing; Shafi'is only require correct timing regardless of number.

Key Terms
بدعت (bid'ah): An innovation in religion that contradicts the established sunnah; here referring to divorcing in a manner not prescribed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why are two divorces in one tuhr considered bid'ah in the Hanafi school?
A) Because the husband did not intend to divorce.
B) Because there is no need (hajat) to combine two divorces in one tuhr.
C) Because the wife was menstruating.
D) Because the divorces were not witnessed.

Key Takeaway
Two divorces in one tuhr are bid'ah (makruh tahrimi) but still legally effective.

One Bain Divorce Without Intercourse: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on one bain divorce without intercourse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the two Hanafi narrations on giving one bain divorce in a tuhr without intercourse and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Imam Muhammad has two narrations: one says it is against Sunnah, the other says no dislikedness due to necessity.

In this lesson, we delve into an intra-Hanafi dispute. The scenario is a husband giving his wife a single bain divorce in a tuhr in which he did not have intercourse. Imam Muhammad reports two different views, one from his book al-Mabsut and another from al-Ziyadat (or Ziyadat al-Ziyadat). We will analyze the reasoning behind each and see which position is relied upon for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the dispute
The scenario: one bain divorce in a tuhr without intercourse. The dispute: is this against the Sunnah (khilaf al-sunnah) or is there no dislike (la karaah)?
Bain divorce is an irrevocable divorce; it differs from raj'i divorce.
2
State Imam Muhammad's view in al-Mabsut
Imam Muhammad in al-Mabsut says it is khilaf al-sunnah, i.e., contrary to the preferred method. The reason: there is no need to add the extra quality of baynunah (irrevocability) when separating from a wife.
This is considered the weaker view in terms of fatwa practice.
3
State the narration in al-Ziyadat
In al-Ziyadat, the narration is that there is no karaah (dislike) in giving one bain divorce without intercourse. The reason: sometimes immediate separation is necessary, and bain divorce achieves that instantly.
This is the view preferred for fatwa due to practical need.
4
Analyze the reasoning behind each
The Mabsut view emphasizes that baynunah is an extra quality not needed; the Ziyadat view acknowledges that necessity (hajat) can justify immediate irrevocability.
This shows the role of necessity in Hanafi rulings.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The mufta bihi (operative position for fatwa) is the Ziyadat view: no karaah. This is due to the prevalence of needs for immediate separation.
Also note the textual issue: Al-Hidayah says 'al-Ziyadat' but the correct source is 'Ziyadat al-Ziyadat'. However, it is considered part of al-Ziyadat.

The author of Al-Hidayah says that giving two divorces in one tuhr is also bid'ah, due to the proof of need for combining. زیادات (Ziyadat): One of the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah by Imam Muhammad, containing additional issues not in the early works.

Definition of Sunnah Divorce in Time and Number
Defines the two aspects of sunnah divorce: time and number, with conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two aspects of sunnah divorce (time and number) and apply the definition to distinguish between the rulings for consummated and non-consummated wives.

Core Idea
Sunnah divorce requires a pure period without intercourse for consummated wives; timing is irrelevant for the unconsummated.

In Hanafi fiqh, divorce (talaq) is classified as sunnah (recommended) or bid'ah (reprehensible innovation). This passage defines the sunnah method from two angles: the correct time (al-waqt) and the correct number (al-'adad). Understanding these conditions is essential for a valid and meritorious divorce. The key distinction is between a wife with whom marriage has been consummated (madkhul biha) and one who has not—because the rationale (the proof of need and genuine desire) differs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two aspects
The sunnah divorce is defined by two separate dimensions: 'sunnah in time' and 'sunnah in number'. Recognize that they are independent conditions.
Sunnah in number applies to all wives equally; sunnah in time applies only to consummated marriages.
2
Define sunnah in time
For the consummated wife, the recommended time is a tuhr (a pure period between menstruations) in which the husband has not had intercourse with her. This ensures the decision is made with renewed desire, not aversion.
Menstruation and intercourse within the same tuhr diminish desire and thus are not suitable for divorce.
3
Define sunnah in number
Sunnah in number means the husband should give three separate divorces over three distinct tuhrs, not all at once. This applies to both consummated and non-consummated wives.
Some schools do not require the number condition; Hanafis insist on it based on the practice of the Prophet ﷺ.
4
Recognize the distinction for non-consummated wives
The time condition is waived for a non-consummated wife. She can be divorced even during menstruation, because her desire is genuine and not affected by menses (her purpose remains unfulfilled).
Imam Zufar disagreed, analogizing her to the consummated wife, but the majority of Hanafis follow the stronger proof: the non-consummated wife's desire is constant.
5
Understand the underlying rationale
The Hanafi proof is based on 'dafil al-hajah' (proof of need). Divorce should occur when the husband's inclination is real and not influenced by transient aversion (like menstruation) or weakened desire (like intercourse in the same tuhr).
This rationale explains why the time condition is limited to consummated marriages.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
طلاق سنت
مینی شرح بدایه )
والسنة في الطلاق من وجهين سنة فى الوقت وسنة فى العدد فالسنة فى العدد يستوى فيها المدخول بها وغير المدخول بها وقد ذكرناها والسنة فى الوقت يثبت في المدخول بها خاصة وهو ان يطلقها في طهر لم يجامعها فيه لان المراعى دليل الحاجة وهو الاقدام على الطلاق في زمان تجدد الرغبة وهو الطهر الخالي عن الجماع آمازمان الحيض فزمان النفرة وبالجماع مرة فى الطهرتفتر الرغبة وغير المدخول بها يطلقها فى حالة الطهر والحيض خلافا لزفر وهو يقيسها على المدخول بهاولنا ان الرغبة في غير المدخول بها صادقة لاتقل بالحيض مالم يحصل مقصوده منها وفى المدخول بها تتجدد بالطهر
ترجمہ اور طلاق میں سنت دو طریقے سے ہے۔ سنت فی الوقت اور سنت فی العدد۔ پس سنت فی العدد اس میں مدخول بہا اور غیر مدخول بہا دونوں برابر ہیں۔ اور ہم نے اس کو ذکر کیا۔ اور سنت فی الوقت خاص طور سے مدخول بہا میں ثابت ہو گی ۔ اور وہ یہ ہے کہ عورت کو ایسے طہر میں طلاق دے جس میں اس کے ساتھ جماع نہیں کیا۔ کیونکہ ملحوظ دلیل حاجت ہے۔ اور وہ (دلیل) طلاق دینے پر اقدام کرنا ہے ایسے زمانہ کہ رغبت نئی ہوتی ہے اور وہ طہر ہے جو جماع سے خالی ہے۔ بہر حال حیض کا زمانہ تو وہ نفرت کا زمانہ ہے۔ اور ایک مرتبہ طہر
Sunnah divorce is from two aspects: sunnah in time and sunnah in number. Sunnah in number applies equally to the consummated and the non-consummated, and we have mentioned it. Sunnah in time is established specifically for the consummated wife, and it is that he divorces her in a tuhr in which he has not had intercourse with her, because the consideration is the proof of need, which is proceeding with divorce at a time when desire is renewed, and that is a tuhr free from intercourse. As for the time of menstruation, it is a time of aversion. And by one instance of intercourse in a tuhr, desire weakens. As for the non-consummated wife, he divorces her in the state of tuhr or menstruation, contrary to Zufar who analogizes her to the consummated wife. Our proof is that desire in the non-consummated wife is genuine and does not diminish with menstruation as long as her purpose is not achieved. In the consummated wife, desire is renewed with tuhr. Translation: And in divorce, sunnah is in two ways: sunnah in time and sunnah in number. So sunnah in number, in this the consummated and non-consummated are equal, and we have mentioned it. And sunnah in time will be established specifically for the consummated wife, and that is that he gives divorce in a tuhr in which he has not had intercourse, because the consideration is the proof of need, and that is proceeding with divorce at a time when desire is renewed, and that is a tuhr free from intercourse. In any case, the time of menstruation is the time of aversion, and once in a tuhr, desire weakens.
Source pages p. 227

Commentary
This passage defines the sunnah method of divorce according to the Hanafi school. It explains that sunnah divorce has two components: sunnah in number and sunnah in time. Sunnah in number means that divorces should be given separately (one per tuhr) for a total of three, and this applies equally to both consummated and unconsummated marriages. Sunnah in time applies only to consummated marriages: divorce should be given during a tuhr (pure period) when the husband has not had intercourse with his wife, because this is the time when desire is renewed and there is genuine inclination. Giving divorce during menstruation is not sunnah because it is a time of aversion. For an unconsummated wife, the time condition does not apply because her desire is not affected by menstruation; she can be divorced even during menstruation, contrary to the opinion of Imam Zufar who analogizes her to the consummated wife. The Hanafi proof is that the unconsummated wife's desire is sincere and not lessened by menstruation since her purpose (consummation) hasn't been achieved.

Key Terms
سنت فی الوقت (sunnah fi al-waqt): The sunnah aspect of divorce that relates to the appropriate time: a tuhr (pure period) without intercourse for consummated marriages.
سنت فی العدد (sunnah fi al-'adad): The sunnah aspect of divorce that relates to the number: giving three divorces separately over three tuhrs, not all at once.
مدخول بہا (madkhul biha): A wife with whom the husband has consummated the marriage; she has a waiting period ('iddah) and specific rules for sunnah divorce.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is true about sunnah divorce for a non-consummated wife?
A) She can only be divorced during a tuhr without intercourse.
B) She can be divorced during any time, including menstruation, because her desire is not affected by menses.
C) She must be divorced three times in one sitting for it to be sunnah.
D) She must have a waiting period of three menstruations before divorce can take effect.

Key Takeaway
Sunnah divorce has two dimensions: time (tuhr without intercourse for consummated wife) and number (one divorce per tuhr for three tuhrs for all wives).

Two Divorces, Talaq Ba'in, and the Principle of External Prohibition
Expansion probe: rebuttal of Shafi'i, ruling on two divorces, and intra-Hanafi dispute on talaq ba'in.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between inherent and external prohibition in Hanafi legal theory, state the ruling that two divorces in one tuhr is bid'ah, and evaluate the two narrations from Imam Muhammad on talaq ba'in to identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Divorce is legitimate, but violating the sunnah makes it prohibited; need (hajat) can justify an irrevocable divorce without dislike.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah weaves together a theoretical rebuttal to Imam Shafi'i, a practical ruling on multiple divorces, and an internal Hanafi debate about the ruling of one talaq ba'in. By tracing the argument, you will learn how Hanafi scholars apply the distinction between inherent and external prohibition, and how they weigh different narrations within the school to arrive at the operative fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Shafi'i objection
The Shafi'i principle states that a legitimate act (mashru') cannot be prohibited. The passage begins by refuting this claim.
Shafi'i's dalil: 'al-mashru'iyyah la tujami' al-hazr'.
2
Analyze the Hanafi distinction
The Hanafi response distinguishes between prohibition inherent in the act (mamnu' li-dhatihi) and prohibition due to an external factor (mamnu' li-ghayrihi). The example of prayer on usurped land illustrates how a legitimate act becomes prohibited externally.
The prayer itself is mashru', but the usurpation makes it mamnu' li-ghayrihi.
3
Apply to the case of two divorces
Divorce in itself is legitimate, but when two divorces are given in one tuhr, it becomes prohibited because it abandons the sunnah of separation and harms marital interests.
The text explicitly says: 'دو طلاق کا ایک طہر میں واقع کرنا بھی بدعت ہے'.
4
Identify the intra-Hanafi dispute on talaq ba'in
If one irrevocable divorce (talaq ba'in) is given in a tuhr without intercourse, two narrations from Imam Muhammad exist: one from al-Mabsut calling it khilaf al-sunnah, and one from al-Ziyadat stating there is no karahah.
Reasoning: in al-Mabsut, baynunah is unnecessary; in al-Ziyadat, immediate need may require it.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The author of al-Hidayah opts for the view from al-Ziyadat due to need (hajat). The citation issue (Ziyadat vs Ziyadat al-Ziyadat) is also clarified by 'Ayni.
The mufta bihi is that there is no karahah in one talaq ba'in in a tuhr without intercourse.

والمشروعية في ذاتہ سے امام شافعی کی بیان کردہ دلیل المشروعية لا تجامع الحظر کا جواب ہے۔ جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ مشروع لذاتہ ممنوع لذاتہ کے ساتھ بلاشبہ جمع نہیں ہو سکتا لیکن مشروع لذاتہ ممنوع لغیرہ کے ساتھ جمع ہوسکتا ہے۔ جیسے ارضِ مخصو بہ میں نماز ادا کرنا اور بیع اذان جمعہ کے وقت کہ نفس نماز اور نفس بیع مشرع ہے لیکن ارض مغصو بہ اور ترک سعی الی الجمعہ کی وجہ سے ممنوع لغیرہ ہے۔ اسی طرح مسئلہ مذکورہ میں نفس طلاق مشروع ہے۔ اور مصالح نکاح فوت ہونے کی وجہ سے ممنوع لغیرہ ہے۔ اسی طرح مسئلہ مذکورہ میں نفس طلاق مشروع ہے۔ اور مصالح نکاح فوت ہونے کی وجہ سے ممنوع لغیرہ ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ دو طلاق کا ایک طہر میں واقع کرنا بھی بدعت ہے۔ دلیل حاجت الی الجمع کی وجہ سے۔ اگر کسی نے اپنی بیوی کو ایک طلاق بائن ایسے طہر میں دی جس میں اسکے ساتھ جماع نہیں کیا گیا تو اس بارے میں ہمارے علماء سے روایات مختلف ہیں۔ چنانچہ امام محمد نے مبسوط میں فرمایا کہ یہ خلاف سنت ہے۔ اسلئے کہ عورت سے چھٹکارا پانے میں بینونت جو صفت زائدہ ہے اس کو ثابت کرنے کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ زیادات میں روایت یہ ہے کہ ایک طلاق بائنہ میں کوئی کراہت نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ بھی فوری چھٹکارے کی ضرورت پیش آجاتی ہے۔ اور فوری چھٹکارا صفت بینونت کے بغیر نہیں ہو سکتا۔ اسلئے اس صفت کو زیادہ کرنے میں کوئی کراہت نہیں۔ سوال .. صاحب ہدایہ کیلئے مناسب یہ تھا کہ فرماتے فی زیادات الزیادات اسلئے کہ امام محمد نے اس مسئلہ کو زیادات الزیادات میں ذکر کیا ہے نہ کہ زیادات میں۔ لیکن جواب میں کہا جا سکتا ہے کہ کاتب سے سہو ہو گیا۔ اور یہ بھی احتمال ہے کہ مصنف ہدایہ نے یہی کہا ہو۔ کیونکہ زیادات الزیادات، زیادات کا ہی تمہ ہے۔ پس زیادات الزیادات کا مسئلہ زیادات ہی کا مسئلہ شمار ہو گا ۔ ( عینی شرح ہدایہ ) فوائد طلاق سنت میں مذاہب کا حاصل یہ ہیکہ ہمارے نزدیک طلاق سنت میں تفریق اور وقت دونوں معتبر ہیں ۔ اور امام مالک کے نزدیک ایک طالق اور وقت معتبر ہے اور امام شافعی کے نزیک صرف وقت معتبر ہے عدد کا اعتبار نہیں ہے ۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب
And this is an answer to Imam Shafi'i's argument that 'mashru'iyyah (legitimacy) does not coincide with prohibition.' The gist of the answer is that something which is legitimate in itself can definitely not coexist with something prohibited in itself, but something legitimate in itself can coexist with something prohibited due to an external factor. For example, performing prayer on usurped land and selling during the call for Friday prayer: the prayer itself and the sale itself are legitimate, but they are prohibited due to the usurped land and abandoning the effort to go to Friday prayer. Similarly, in the mentioned case, the divorce itself is legitimate, but it is prohibited due to the loss of the benefits of marriage. Sahib al-Hidayah says: Effecting two divorces in one tuhr is also bid'ah, due to the evidence of the need for combination. If a man gave his wife one irrevocable divorce (talaq ba'in) in a tuhr in which he did not have intercourse with her, then there are different narrations from our scholars. Imam Muhammad said in al-Mabsut that this is against the sunnah, because in getting rid of the woman, there is no need to establish the added quality of irrevocability. In al-Ziyadat, the narration is that there is no dislike in one irrevocable divorce, because sometimes an immediate need for separation arises, and immediate separation cannot be achieved without the quality of irrevocability. Therefore, there is no dislike in adding this quality. Question: It would have been appropriate for Sahib al-Hidayah to say 'in Ziyadat al-Ziyadat', because Imam Muhammad mentioned this issue in Ziyadat al-Ziyadat, not in al-Ziyadat. But in answer, it can be said that there was a scribal error, and it is also possible that the author of al-Hidayah said it because Ziyadat al-Ziyadat is part of al-Ziyadat. Thus, the issue of Ziyadat al-Ziyadat is considered part of al-Ziyadat (Ayni Sharh al-Hidayah). Summary of the schools on sunnah divorce: According to us, both separation and time are considered in sunnah divorce; according to Imam Malik, one divorce and time are considered; according to Imam Shafi'i, only time is considered, not the number. And Allah knows best what is correct.
Source pages p. 227

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from Ashraf al-Hidayah that addresses several interconnected rulings. First, it rebuts a Shafi'i argument that a legitimate act cannot coexist with prohibition; the Hanafi response distinguishes between inherent and external prohibition. Then, it states that giving two divorces in one tuhr is bid'ah (an innovation), as it violates the sunnah of spacing divorces. Next, it discusses an intra-Hanafi dispute: if a man gives one irrevocable divorce (talaq ba'in) in a tuhr without intercourse, there are two narrations from Imam Muhammad. In al-Mabsut, he says it is against the sunnah because the irrevocability (baynunah) is unnecessary; but in al-Ziyadat, he says there is no dislike because immediate separation may be needed. The author also clarifies a citation issue: Imam Muhammad mentioned this in Ziyadat al-Ziyadat, not in al-Ziyadat, but the author of al-Hidayah considered them the same. Finally, the passage summarizes the positions of the three madhahib on sunnah divorce: Hanafi requires both correct separation (one per tuhr) and correct time (tuhr without intercourse); Maliki requires one divorce and correct time; Shafi'i requires only correct time, not number.

Key Terms
طلاق بائن (talaq ba'in): An irrevocable divorce that separates the couple immediately without the possibility of revocation during the 'iddah.
بدعت (bid'ah): An innovation in religious practice that goes against the sunnah; here it refers to a disliked or prohibited act.
حاجت (hajat): Need; the necessity that allows a legal concession. Here it is the basis for the permissibility of talaq ba'in.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position on giving one talaq ba'in in a tuhr without intercourse?
A) It is khilaf al-sunnah (against the sunnah).
B) It is bid'ah (innovation).
C) There is no karahah (dislike) because of need.
D) It is haram (prohibited).

Key Takeaway
A legitimate act can be prohibited due to external factors; two divorces in one tuhr is bid'ah, but one talaq ba'in in a tuhr is permissible without dislike if need requires it.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
8 min
Sunnah Divorce: Time, Number, and the Dispute with Imam Zufar
Definition of sunnah talaq in time and number, with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two aspects of sunnah in talaq, distinguish their application to consummated vs non-consummated wives, and evaluate Imam Zufar's qiyas-based objection.

Core Idea
Sunnah in time is for consummated wives only; non-consummated wives may be divorced any time, even during menstruation.

Divorce in Islam is not left unrestricted; the Shari'ah has prescribed a sunnah method that preserves dignity and allows for reconciliation. This lesson unpacks the two dimensions of sunnah in talaq — time and number — and clarifies a key intra-Hanafi dispute: can a non-consummated wife be divorced while menstruating? By understanding the underlying principle of 'evidence of need' (dalīl al-ḥājah), you will see why the majority of Hanafi imams permit it, contrary to Imam Zufar's qiyas.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on sunnah in time
Identify that the sunnah in time (divorcing in a tuhr without intercourse) is required only for a consummated wife (madkhul bihā). For a non-consummated wife (ghayr madkhul bihā), there is no such condition.
2
Identify Imam Zufar's objection
Imam Zufar analogizes the non-consummated wife to the consummated one, arguing that menstruation is a time of aversion in both cases, making divorce during menstruation makruh tahrimi.
3
Follow Zufar's qiyas
His analogy: the 'illa (effective cause) is the aversion caused by menstruation, which applies to all wives. Therefore, divorce should be avoided in that state for both.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The majority rejects the qiyas because the 'illa differs: in a consummated wife, desire is renewed after tuhr, so divorce during menstruation violates the need-based rationale. In a non-consummated wife, desire remains constant regardless of menstruation, so the evidence of need (dalīl al-ḥājah) exists even during menses.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: according to the majority, divorcing a non-consummated wife during menstruation is mubah (permissible, no karahah). According to Zufar, it is makruh tahrimi.
The mufta bihi is the majority position.

مدخول بہا اور غیر مدخول بہا دونوں کو عام ہے۔ جواب یہ ہے کہ اسی حدیث میں ایک روایت ہے فتلک العدة التي امر الله تعالى ان يطلق لها النساء یعنی یہ وہ عدت ہے جس کا اللہ نے حکم فرمایا کہ اس وقت پر عورتیں طلاق دی جائیں اور عدت صرف مدخول بہا کیلئے ہوتی ہے نہ کہ غیر مدخول بہا کیلئے۔ پس معلوم ہوا کہ حدیث ابن عمر مدخول بہا کے ساتھ خاص ہے۔ لہذا اس حدیث کو لے کر اعتراض نہ کیا جائے۔
And the sunnah in divorce is from two aspects: sunnah in time and sunnah in number. The sunnah in number is equal for the consummated wife and the non-consummated wife, and we have mentioned it. The sunnah in time is established specifically for the consummated wife, and it is that he divorces her in a state of purity (tuhr) in which he has not had intercourse with her, because the consideration is the evidence of need, which is proceeding to divorce in a time of renewed desire, and that is the purity free from intercourse. As for the time of menstruation, it is a time of aversion, and by engaging in intercourse once in the purity, desire weakens. And the non-consummated wife is divorced in the state of purity and menstruation, contrary to Zufar, who analogizes her to the consummated wife. Our evidence is that desire in the non-consummated wife is genuine, not diminished by menstruation, as long as her intended purpose (of marriage) has not been achieved. Translation: And in divorce, the sunnah is in two ways: sunnah in time and sunnah in number. So sunnah in number: the consummated and non-consummated are equal. And we have mentioned it. And sunnah in time is specifically established for the consummated wife, and it is that he divorces her in a purity in which he has not had intercourse, because the considered thing is the evidence of need, which is proceeding to divorce at a time when desire is renewed, and that is the purity free from intercourse. In any case, the time of menstruation is a time of aversion, and once in the purity, by having intercourse, desire weakens. And the non-consummated wife, he divorces her in the time of purity and menstruation, contrary to Imam Zufar, who analogizes her to the consummated wife. And our evidence is that desire in the non-consummated wife is complete, it does not decrease due to menstruation, until her intended purpose is achieved. And in the consummated wife, desire is renewed due to purity. Elaboration: The author divided the sunnah in divorce. He said that the sunnah in divorce has two types: one is sunnah in time and one is sunnah in number. Sunnah in number is that the woman should be given only one divorce in one purity, as has passed in the first chapter. And in this, the consummated and non-consummated are equal. And sunnah in time is specifically established for the consummated wife. And sunnah in time is that the man gives divorce to the woman in a purity that is free from intercourse. The evidence is that the legitimacy of divorce is due to need, and the evidence of need is proceeding to divorce at a time of renewed desire, and the time of renewed desire is the purity that is free from intercourse. And the time of menstruation is a time of aversion, and once in the purity, by having intercourse, desire weakens. So in the state of menstruation and in the purity in which intercourse has occurred, the evidence of need is not present such that divorce can be considered legitimate as a substitute for need. Therefore we said that sunnah in time is only that divorce is given in purity, not in the state of menstruation, and that purity is free from intercourse. As for the case of the non-consummated wife, she can be divorced in both purity and menstruation. Imam Zufar says that divorcing the non-consummated wife in the state of menstruation is makruh tahrimi. Imam Zufar analogizes the non-consummated to the consummated. Our evidence is that desire in the non-consummated is fully present, it does not decrease due to menstruation, until that non-consummated wife achieves her intended purpose. Therefore, the husband's action of divorcing the non-consummated wife in menstruation will be due to need, not due to aversion. And in the consummated, due to purity, since desire is renewed, therefore divorcing the consummated in a purity free from intercourse is permissible. Benefits: Here there is an objection: the author said that divorcing the non-consummated wife during menstruation is correct, while the hadith of Ibn Umar says, 'The sunnah is to wait for purity.' This hadith, by its generality, covers both the consummated and non-consummated. The answer is that in the same hadith there is a narration: 'That is the 'iddah which Allah has commanded that women be divorced for.' And 'iddah is only for the consummated wife, not for the non-consummated. So it becomes known that the hadith of Ibn Umar is specific to the consummated wife. Therefore, objection should not be raised based on this hadith.
Source pages p. 227

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah provides a detailed explanation of the two aspects of sunnah divorce: sunnah in number (one divorce per tuhr, applicable to all wives) and sunnah in time (specific to consummated wives: divorce in a tuhr without intercourse). The reasoning is based on the principle of 'dalil al-hajah' (evidence of need): divorce is legitimate only when there is a genuine need, indicated by a renewal of desire (raghbah) which occurs in a tuhr free from intercourse. Menstruation indicates aversion, and intercourse in the tuhr diminishes desire, so divorce at those times is not sunnah. For non-consummated wives, however, desire remains strong regardless of menstruation because their marital relationship has not been fulfilled. Imam Zufar differed, analogizing all wives, but the majority of Hanafi scholars maintain the distinction. The passage also resolves the objection from the hadith of Ibn Umar that seems to require waiting for purity for all wives: the hadith is qualified by another narration stating that 'iddah is only for consummated wives, so it applies only to them. Thus, the sunnah in time is specific to consummated wives.

Key Terms
سنة الوقت (sunnat al-waqt): The sunnah condition of time for divorce: it must be given in a state of purity (tuhr) without intercourse, for a consummated wife.
سنة العدد (sunnat al-'adad): The sunnah condition of number: only one divorce should be given in one tuhr.
غير مدخول بها (ghayr madkhul biha): A wife with whom the husband has not yet consummated the marriage.
دليل الحاجة (dalil al-hajah): The evidence of need: the situation must indicate genuine necessity for divorce, shown by renewed desire.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school permit divorcing a non-consummated wife during menstruation?
A) Because she does not observe 'iddah
B) Because desire in her is not diminished by menstruation
C) Because all wives are equal in this matter
D) Because menstruation is a pure time

Key Takeaway
Sunnah in time (tuhr without intercourse) is only required for consummated wives; non-consummated wives may be divorced at any time, including during menstruation, due to the constant presence of need (dalīl al-ḥājah).

Sunnah Divorce for a Non-Menstruating Woman
Ruling on the sunnah method of divorce for a non-menstruating woman

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah method of divorce for a non-menstruating woman and apply the rule of substituting the month for menstruation in both divorce spacing and 'iddah.

Core Idea
The month replaces menstruation for both divorce spacing and 'iddah.

Divorce according to the sunnah is a precisely timed act. For a woman who menstruates, the sunnah instructs the husband to divorce her in a tuhr (pure state) without intercourse. But what if she does not menstruate at all, due to youth or menopause? The Hanafi school answers this by turning to the month as the key unit, directly from the Quran. This lesson unpacks that substitution and its practical application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject
The ruling applies to a woman who does not menstruate, either because she is pre-pubescent (saghar) or post-menopausal (kubr).
In Hanafi fiqh, the minimum age for menstruation is usually 9; menopause is typically around 55.
2
State the sunnah method
If a husband intends to give three divorces following the sunnah, he gives one divorce, then waits a month, then gives the second, then waits another month, then the third.
This spacing mirrors the inter-menstrual interval for a menstruating woman.
3
Locate the proof
The proof is from Surah al-Talaq 65:4, which sets the 'iddah for non-menstruating women as three months, establishing the month as the unit of time.
The verse says: 'And those who have despaired of menstruation... their 'iddah is three months, and those who have not menstruated.'
4
Apply the method of counting
If the divorce is at the beginning of a lunar month, count by lunar months (29/30 days). If in the middle, count by full calendar days (30 days per month).
This distinction prevents ambiguity when the lunar month does not align with the date of divorce.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عورت کو حیض صغر یا کبر کی وجہ سے نہ آتا ہو اس کیلئے طلاق کا سنت طریقہ قال واذا كانت المرأة لا تحيض من صغر او كبر فارادان يطلقها ثلثا للسنة طلقها واحدة فاذا مضى شهر طلقها اخرى لان الشهر في حقها قائم مقام الحيض قال الله تعالى واللائى ينسن من المحيض الى ان قال و الائى لم يحضن والاقامة فى الحيض خاصة حتى يقدر الاستبراء فى حقها بالشهر وهو بالحيض لا بالطهر ثم ان كان الطلاق في اول الشهر يعتبر الشهور بالاهلة وانكان فى وسطه فبالايام في حق التفريق و في حق العدة
For a woman who does not menstruate due to young age or old age, the sunnah method of divorce is: He said, 'And when a woman does not menstruate due to young age or old age, and he intends to divorce her three times according to the sunnah, he divorces her once, then when a month passes, he divorces her once more, because the month in her case stands in place of menstruation. Allah Almighty said: 'And those who have despaired of menstruation...until He said: 'and those who have not menstruated.' And the stay in menstruation is specific, so that waiting period (istibra') in her case is estimated by the month, and it is by menstruation, not by purity. Then, if the divorce is at the beginning of the month, months are considered by the lunar calendars, and if it is in the middle, then by days in terms of separation and in terms of 'iddah.
Source pages p. 228

Commentary
This passage is a matn (concise ruling) from the classical Hanafi text, likely from al-Hidayah or similar, explaining the sunnah method for a woman who does not menstruate. Such a woman could be either pre-pubescent (saghar) or post-menopausal (kubr). Since menstruation is the natural time indicator for divorce and 'iddah, the month (approximately 30 days) takes its place. The sunnah is to give one divorce per month, spacing them out. The evidence is from the Quranic verses (65:4) mentioning those who have despaired of menstruation and those who have not menstruated. The 'iddah for such women is three months. The text also distinguishes between divorcing at the beginning of a month (use lunar months) versus in the middle (use days from the date of divorce).

Key Terms
صغر (saghar): Young age where a girl has not yet reached menarche.
كبر (kubr): Old age where a woman has reached menopause and no longer menstruates.
شهر (shahr): A month; in legal terms, it can be a lunar month (29 or 30 days) or 30 days counted from the date.
استبراء (istibra'): A waiting period to ensure a woman is not pregnant; here it refers to the 'iddah period.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) After one lunar month, i.e., on the 1st of Dhu al-Qa'dah
B) After 30 days, i.e., on the 1st of Dhu al-Qa'dah (counting by days)
C) After she shows signs of pregnancy
D) Immediately, because she cannot menstruate

Key Takeaway
For a non-menstruating woman, the month replaces menstruation as the time unit for both sunnah divorce spacing and 'iddah, with counting method depending on whether the divorce is at the start or middle of a month.

Talaq of a Non-Consummated Wife During Menstruation
Explaining permissibility with proof and refuting Imam Zufar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on divorcing a non-consummated wife during menstruation and distinguish it from the ruling for a consummated wife based on the concept of need (hajat).

Core Idea
Desire determines need: a non-consummated wife's desire is constant, so talaq during menstruation is valid.

In this lesson, we explore an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the permissibility of divorcing a wife who has not been consummated (ghayr madkhul biha) during her menstrual period. The majority of Hanafi imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) allow it, while Imam Zufar considers it makruh tahrimi. We will examine the rational proof based on the concept of 'hajat' (need) and how the timing of desire dictates the ruling. The text also clarifies the distinction between sunnah fi al-waqt and sunnah fi al-adad, and addresses an objection from the hadith of Ibn Umar.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi majority position
Identify what the majority of Hanafi scholars (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) hold regarding talaq of a non-consummated wife during menstruation. The ruling is mubah (permissible), not makruh.
2
Identify the intra-Hanafi opponent and their proof
Imam Zufar holds it is makruh tahrimi. His proof is qiyas (analogy) with a consummated wife, where talaq during menstruation is prohibited. Identify the basis of his analogy.
Imam Zufar is a prominent Hanafi scholar, but his view is overruled by the majority.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response and rebuttal
The majority respond that the analogy fails because the effective cause (illa) for prohibition in a consummated wife is the absence of need (desire is diminished). In a non-consummated wife, desire remains full, so need exists, making talaq permissible.
This is a classic case of tahqiq al-manat: the illa is not present in the far'.
4
Apply the distinction between sunnah fi al-waqt and sunnah fi al-adad
Sunnah fi al-adad (giving one talaq per tuhr) applies to both consummated and non-consummated wives. Sunnah fi al-waqt (timing in a pure state free from intercourse) applies only to consummated wives. Understand why.
For a non-consummated wife, the timing condition is irrelevant because she has no iddah and her desire is constant.
5
Address the potential objection from the hadith of Ibn Umar
The hadith commands waiting for tuhr before divorce, but it is restricted to consummated wives because it mentions iddah, which applies only to them. Thus, it does not affect a non-consummated wife.
This demonstrates the Hanafi method of takhsis (restricting a general text) using another part of the same hadith.
