In the Book of Talaq: By engaging in intercourse, desire becomes weak. And for a non-consummated wife, he gives her talaq in the time of purity (tuhr). And during menstruation, there is a difference with Imam Zufar. He analogizes her to a consummated wife. Our proof is that in a non-consummated wife, desire is complete; it is not diminished by menstruation, until her purpose is attained from her. And in a consummated wife, due to purity, desire is renewed. Commentary: The author divided sunnah in talaq into two types: sunnah fi al-waqt and sunnah fi al-adad. Sunnah fi al-adad is to give only one talaq in one tuhr, as passed in the first chapter, and in this, consummated and non-consummated are equal. Sunnah fi al-waqt is specific to a consummated wife, and it is that a man gives talaq to his wife in a tuhr that is free from intercourse. The proof is that legislation of talaq is due to need. And [the indication] of need is a proof. And the proof of need is action upon talaq in a time of desire. And the time of desire is the tuhr that is free from intercourse. As for the time of menstruation, it is a time of aversion. And in a tuhr, once intercourse occurs, desire decreases. So in the state of menstruation and in the tuhr in which intercourse occurred, the proof of need is not present such that talaq can be legislated by placing it as a substitute for need. Therefore we said that sunnah fi al-waqt is only that talaq be given in a tuhr, not in the state of menstruation, and that tuhr be free from intercourse. As for the case of a non-consummated wife, she can be divorced in both tuhr and menstruation. Imam Zufar says that giving talaq to a non-consummated wife during menstruation is makruh tahrimi. Imam Zufar analogizes a non-consummated wife to a consummated one. Our proof is that in a non-consummated wife, desire remains full, not diminished by menstruation, until her purpose is attained from her. So the husband's action of giving talaq to a non-consummated wife during menstruation is due to need, not due to aversion. And for a consummated wife, because desire is renewed due to purity, giving talaq in a tuhr free from intercourse is mubah. Benefits: Here is an objection: The author said that giving talaq to a non-consummated wife during menstruation is valid, whereas the hadith of Ibn Umar says: 'Indeed the sunnah is to wait for the tuhr,' and this hadith, by its generality, includes both consummated and non-consummated. The answer is that in the same hadith there is a narration: 'That is the iddah which Allah commanded that women be divorced for it,' and iddah is only for a consummated wife, not for a non-consummated wife. So it is known that the hadith of Ibn Umar is specific to a consummated wife. Therefore, this hadith should not be used to object.
Source pages p. 228

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the ruling of divorcing a non-consummated wife (ghayr madkhul biha) during menstruation. The author first explains the concept of sunnah in talaq, dividing it into sunnah fi al-waqt (timing) and sunnah fi al-adad (number). For a consummated wife (madkhul biha), the sunnah method requires talaq in a state of purity (tuhr) free from intercourse, because desire is renewed after a period of purity, and talaq is legislated due to need. During menstruation, desire is absent, so talaq is not sunnah. However, for a non-consummated wife, desire remains constant and is not diminished by menstruation. Therefore, talaq is permissible even during menstruation. Imam Zufar (a Hanafi scholar) disagrees, analogizing her to a consummated wife, and holds it is makruh tahrimi. The Hanafi majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) hold that it is valid and not makruh tahrimi. The text then addresses an objection from the hadith of Ibn Umar, which seems to require waiting for tuhr. The answer is that the same hadith specifies iddah, which only applies to consummated wives, thus the ruling is restricted to them. Therefore, the hadith does not apply to a non-consummated wife.

Key Terms
سنت فی الوقت (sunnah fi al-waqt): The sunnah method regarding timing of talaq: giving talaq in a state of purity (tuhr) free from intercourse.
سنت فی العدد (sunnah fi al-adad): The sunnah method regarding number of talaq: giving only one talaq in one tuhr.
غیر مدخول بہا (ghayr madkhul biha): A wife who has not been consummated; no sexual intercourse has occurred.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on divorcing a non-consummated wife (ghayr madkhul biha) during menstruation?
A) It is prohibited (haram).
B) It is permissible (ja'iz).
C) It is makruh tahrimi.
D) It is invalid (batil).

Key Takeaway
A non-consummated wife may be divorced during menstruation because her desire remains constant, fulfilling the need that justifies talaq.

Sunnah Talaq for Non-Menstruating Women and the Month Counting Dispute
Setting the rules for sunnah talaq when a woman does not menstruate, and intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on counting months

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for sunnah talaq of a non-menstruating woman and explain the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on counting months.

Core Idea
For a non-menstruating woman, the month substitutes for menstruation in iddah and istibra', but the method of counting months differs between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples.

When a woman does not menstruate due to youth or old age, the Hanafi school prescribes a sunnah method for divorce: one talaq per month over three months, based on Quran 65:4. However, a key intra-madhhab dispute arises when the first talaq is given in the middle of a month — should the months be counted by lunar crescents or by 30-day periods? This lesson unpacks the ruling, its proof, and the ikhtilaf between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the Hanafi ruling on sunnah talaq for a non-menstruating woman: one talaq per month for three months.
The month stands in place of menstruation for legal purposes.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the Quranic proof: Surah al-Talaq 65:4, which sets iddah as three months for those who do not menstruate.
The verse explicitly substitutes months for menstruation.
3
Understand the scope of substitution
Recognize that the substitution is specific to iddah and istibra', not for all rulings (e.g., prohibition of talaq).
The month is legally treated as menstruation only for counting periods.
4
Analyze the first objection and response
Consider the objection that talaq in such a month would be prohibited. Answer: The month is actually purity, but legally substitutes for menstruation only for iddah/istibra'.
The substitute is not identical in every respect.
5
Examine the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Differentiate between Abu Hanifa's view (count months by 30 days) and the Sahibayn's view (first/last months completed by crescent, intermediate by lunar months).
The same ikhtilaf applies to ijarah contracts.

میں ) تو اس کو ایک طلق دے دے۔ پس جب ایک ماہ گذر گیا تو اس کو دوسری طلاق دے دے۔ اسلئے کہ مہیندان دونوں کے حق میں حیض کے قائم مقام ہے۔ اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا اور وہ عورتیں جو حیض سے مایوس ہو گئیں یہاں تک کہ کہا اور وہ عورتیں جن کو حیض نہیں آتا۔ اور قائم کرنا خاص کر حیض میں ہے حتی کہ ان دونوں کے حق میں استبراء کا اندازہ لگایا جائے گا۔ مہینہ کے ساتھ حالانکہ استبراء حیض کے ذریعہ ہوتا ہے۔ اگر وسط ماہ میں ہے تو تفریق کے حق میں ایام کے ذریعہ ہو گا۔ اور ایسا ہی عدت کے حق میں ۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک اور صاحبین کے نزدیک اول مکمل ہو گا آخر ماہ سے اور درمیان کے دو ماہ چاندوں سے اور یہ مسئلہ اجارات کا ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی عورت کو حیض نہ آتا ہو بچپنے کی وجہ سے یا بڑھاپے کی وجہ سے۔ اور اس کا شوہر چاہتا ہے کہ اس کو سنت طریقہ پر تین طالق دے دے تو اس کا حکم یہ ہے کہ تین ماہ میں متفرق طور پر تین طلاق دے دے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ مہینہ صغیرہ اور کبیرہ دونوں کے حق میں حیض کے قائم مقام ہے۔ کیونکہ خدا وند قدوس نے فرمایا واللائي ينسن من المحيض من نسائكم ان ارتبتم فعدتهن ثلاثة اشهر واللائى لم يحضن مطلب یہ ہے کہ اگر تم پر ان دونوں قسم کی عورتوں کی عدت کا حکم مشتبہ ہو جائے تو ان کا حکم یہ ہے کہ تین ماہ عدت گزار ہیں۔ اس آیت سے معلوم ہوا کہ اگر ان عورتوں کو حیض آتا تو ان کی عدت تین حیض ہوتے ۔ مگر چونکہ ان کو حیض ہیں آرہا ہے اسے ان کی عدت تین ماہ ہو گی۔ پس ثابت ہو گیا کہ مہینہ حیض کے قائم مقام ہے۔ والاقامة في الحیض سے احناف کے مذہب مختار کو ذکر کیا ہے کہ مہینہ خاص طور سے حیض کے قائم مقام ہے نہ کہ حیض اور طہر دونوں کے قائم مقام ۔ جیسا کہ دوسرے بعض کی رائے ہے اور شمس الائمہ نے کہا کہ بعض حضرات کی رائے یہ ہے کہ غیر ذوات الحیض کے حق میں مہینہ حیض کے مرتبہ میں ہے اور ذوات الحیض کے حق میں طہر کے مرتبہ میں۔ حالانکہ ایسا نہیں بلکہ اس کے حق میں بھی مہینہ حیض ہی کے مرتبہ میں ہے۔ مذہب مختار کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ باندی جس کو صفر یا کبر کی وجہ سے حیض نہیں آتا۔ اگر انتقال ملک وغیرہ کی وجہ سے اس سے استبراء کرانا ہے تو وہ استبراء اس باندی کے حق میں مہینہ کے ساتھ مقدر کیا جاتا ہے۔ حالانکہ استبراء حیض کے ذریعہ ہوتا ہے۔ نہ کہ طہر کے ذریعہ۔ پس اس سے بھی یہ ثابت ہوا کہ مہینہ صرف حیض کے قائم مقام ہوتا ہے نہ کہ حیض اور طہر دونوں کے۔ اس تقریر پر اشکال ہو گا۔ وہ یہ کہ جب مہینہ حیض کے قائم مقام ہے تو جب بھی ان مہینوں میں سے کسی مہینہ میں طلاق دے گا تو وہ طلاق حیض میں ہوگی ۔ اور یہ حرام ہے جیسا کہ حالت حیض میں۔ دوسرا اشکال یہ ہے کہ جب مہینہ حیض کے قائم مقام ہے تو تین حیض کی جگہ تین ماہ کی کیا ضرورت ہے۔ اسلئے کہ حیض کی اکثر مدت دس دن ہے۔ اور تین حیض کی مدت ایک ماہ میں حاصل ہو جائے گی ۔ پس تین حیض کے قائم مقام ایک ماہ ہونا چاہئے نہ کہ تین ماہ ۔ پہلے اشکال کے جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ یہ مدت (شہر) حقیقۂ طہر ہے لیکن حیض کے قائم مقام ہے اور جو چیز کسی شی ء نے قائم مقام ہو ممکن نہیں کہ وہ من کل وجہ اس کے معنی میں ہو ورنہ تو وہ عین شی ہوگی نہ کہ قائم مقام ۔ پس مہینہ کا قائم مقام ہونا صرف عدت گزارنے اور استبراء کیلئے ہے نہ کہ کسی اور اعجا ر ہے۔ لہذا اب یہ اشکال واقع نہیں ہوگا کہ جب مہینہ حیض کے قائم مقام ہے تو مہینہ میں
He said: And when a woman does not menstruate due to youth or old age, and he intends to give her three talaqs according to sunnah, he gives her one talaq. Then when a month passes, he gives her another, because the month in her case stands in place of menstruation. Allah said: 'And those who have despaired of menstruation... until He said: 'and those who have not menstruated.' And the establishment (iqaamah) is specifically in menstruation, so that istibra' in her case is estimated by the month, and it is by menstruation, not by purity. Then if the talaq is at the beginning of the month, the months are considered by the lunar months, and if in the middle, then by days regarding separation (tafriq) and regarding iddah. Likewise according to Abu Hanifa, and according to the two (Sahibayn), the first is completed by the last, and the two middle ones by the lunar months, and this is the issue of ijarah. Translation: Al-Quduri said: And when a woman does not menstruate due to youth or old age, then he intends to give her three talaqs (at the time of sunnah), he gives her one talaq. Then when a month passes, he gives her a second talaq, because the month for both of them stands in place of menstruation. Allah said: 'And those who have despaired of menstruation... until He said: 'and those who have not menstruated.' And the establishment (iqaamah) is specifically in menstruation, so that istibra' for them is estimated by the month, while istibra' is by menstruation. If it is in the middle of the month, then regarding separation (tafriq) it is by days, and similarly regarding iddah. According to Abu Hanifa, and according to the two (Sahibayn), the first is completed by the last, and the two middle ones by lunar months, and this is the issue of ijarah. Explanation: The issue is that if a woman does not menstruate due to youth or old age, and her husband wants to give her three talaqs according to the sunnah method, the ruling is that he gives three talaqs separately over three months. The proof is that the month for both the young and old woman stands in place of menstruation, because Allah said: 'And those who have despaired of menstruation from among your women, if you doubt, then their iddah is three months, and also those who have not menstruated.' The meaning is that if you are uncertain about the ruling of iddah for these two types of women, their ruling is that they observe iddah for three months. From this verse, it is known that if these women menstruated, their iddah would be three menstruations, but since they do not menstruate, their iddah is three months. So it is established that the month stands in place of menstruation. 'And the establishment (iqaamah) in menstruation' refers to the preferred view (madhhab mukhtar) of the Hanafis that the month specifically stands in place of menstruation, not both menstruation and purity, as some others hold. And Shams al-A'imma said that some scholars hold that for non-menstruating women, the month is in the place of menstruation, and for menstruating women, it is in the place of purity. But this is not correct; rather, for her too, the month is in the place of menstruation. The proof of the preferred view is that for a slave-girl who does not menstruate due to youth or old age, if istibra' is required from her due to transfer of ownership etc., that istibra' is estimated by the month, although istibra' is by menstruation, not by purity. So this also proves that the month only stands in place of menstruation, not both. An objection arises: When the month stands in place of menstruation, then whenever he gives talaq in any of these months, that talaq would be during menstruation, and this is haram, just like during menstruation. A second objection: When the month stands in place of menstruation, then why is there a need for three months instead of three menstruations? Since most menstruations are ten days, three menstruations would be completed in one month. So three menstruations should be replaced by one month, not three. The gist of the answer to the first objection is that this period (the month) is actually the essence of purity (haqiqah al-tuhr), but it stands in place of menstruation. And something that stands in place of something cannot be identical to it in every respect; otherwise it would be that very thing, not a substitute. So the month being a substitute is only for the purpose of completing iddah and istibra', not for any other purpose. Therefore, this objection does not arise that when the month stands in place of menstruation, then in the month...
Source pages p. 228

Commentary
This passage deals with the ruling of giving sunnah talaq to a woman who does not menstruate due to youth (saghir) or old age (kabir). According to the Hanafi school, the month (shahr) serves as a substitute for menstruation for such women, based on the Quranic verse (65:4) that sets the iddah for such women as three months. Therefore, to give sunnah talaq, the husband should give one talaq in each of three consecutive months, analogous to waiting for three menstrual cycles. The text then explains the preferred Hanafi view (madhhab mukhtar) that the month stands specifically in place of menstruation, not both menstruation and purity. Evidence is drawn from the practice of istibra' (waiting period for a slave-girl after transfer of ownership), which is by one month, not by two. The passage then presents two objections to this view and answers them. The first objection is that if the month stands for menstruation, then any talaq given in that month would be in a state of menstruation, which is prohibited. The answer is that the month is actually a period of purity (tuhr) in reality, but it is assigned the legal status of menstruation only for the purposes of iddah and istibra', not for all rulings. The second objection is that three menstruations could be completed in one month, so one month should suffice. The answer is not fully given due to the cut-off. Later, the passage mentions an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) regarding how to count the months when the first talaq is given in the middle of the month. According to Abu Hanifa, each month is counted by days (30 days each), so the first month ends 30 days after the talaq, the second after another 30, etc. According to the Sahibayn, the first and last months are completed by the end of the lunar month, and the intermediate months are counted by lunar months. This ikhtilaf is noted as also applying to ijarah (hire contracts).

Key Terms
قائم مقام حیض (qa'im maqam al-hayd): The month stands in place of menstruation for legal purposes such as iddah and istibra'.
استبراء (istibra'): A waiting period for a slave-girl after change of ownership to ensure she is not pregnant.
اجارات (ijarat): The issue of hire contracts, where similar counting of months is disputed between Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when a husband divorces a non-menstruating woman in the middle of a month, how does Abu Hanifa calculate the next month for giving the second talaq?
A) By the lunar crescent
B) By counting 30 days from the talaq
C) By completing the lunar month then starting anew
D) By waiting until the end of the current lunar month

Key Takeaway
The month serves as a substitute for menstruation only for the purposes of iddah and istibra', not for all rulings, leading to a legitimate intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on the method of counting months.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
15 min
Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Counting Months for 'Iddah of Non-Menstruating Woman
Explains the ruling of divorcing a non-menstruating woman and the method of counting months for 'iddah, with an intra-Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi intra-madhhab dispute regarding counting months for the 'iddah of a non-menstruating woman and apply the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
A month substitutes for menstruation only for 'iddah and istibra', not for divorce timing – a substitute is not identical in every aspect.

This lesson delves into a nuanced issue within Hanafi fiqh: how to count the 'iddah months for a woman who does not menstruate due to youth or old age. The passage from Al-Hidayah presents the evidence from the Quran and the reasoning that a month stands in place of a menstrual period. It then introduces an intra-madhhab disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two students (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) on whether months are counted by days or by lunar months when the divorce occurs in the middle of a month. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to apply Hanafi legal principles and recognize the operative fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the foundational ruling and its evidence
Start by understanding that for a non-menstruating woman, the 'iddah is three months based on Quran 65:4. The month substitutes for menstruation, as established by the Hanafi madhhab. Note the specific proof (istibra' by month) that this substitution is only for menstruation, not purity.
The substitution is only for 'iddah and istibra', not for other rulings like the prohibition of divorcing during menstruation.
2
Outline the intra-Hanafi dispute
When the divorce is given in the middle of a month, Imam Abu Hanifa holds that all months are counted by days (30 days each), resulting in a 90-day 'iddah. The Sahibayn hold that the first month is completed by the remaining days of that month plus some days from the last month, and the middle two months are counted by lunar months (29 or 30 days).
The dispute only arises when divorce occurs mid-month; if at the beginning, all agree lunar months apply.
3
Address the two objections and their answers
The text raises two objections: (1) If a month substitutes for menstruation, divorcing in that month would be like divorcing during menstruation (haram). (2) If one month substitutes for one menstruation, three months should substitute for three menstruations, but three menstruations could fit in one month. The answers clarify that substitution is limited to 'iddah and istibra', and that months substitute for the entire 'iddah period, not the duration of individual menstruations.
These answers reinforce the principle that a legal substitute does not carry all attributes of the original.
4
Identify the mufta bihi position
The text explicitly states 'the fatwa is on the saying of the two', meaning the Sahibayn's view is the operative ruling. Thus, for a mid-month divorce, the 'iddah is calculated by completing the first month with days, then two lunar months.
The example given: if divorce on 15th of a 29-day month, then 4 days remain of that month, plus 6 days of the last month (to make 30 days for the first month), then two full lunar months.
5
Apply the ruling to a concrete scenario
Practice by taking a scenario: A husband divorces his 11-year-old wife (who has not menstruated) on the 10th of Muharram (a 30-day month). According to the mufta bihi, the first month is completed by the remaining 21 days of Muharram plus 9 days of Safar (to make 30 days for the first month), then Rabi' al-Awwal and Rabi' al-Akhir as lunar months. Her 'iddah ends when Rabi' al-Akhir completes.
Always check whether the divorce is at the beginning or middle of a lunar month.

حیض کے قائم مقام ایک ماہ ہونا چاہئے نہ کہ تین ماہ ۔ پہلے اشکال کے جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ یہ مدت (شہر) حقیقۂ طہر ہے لیکن حیض کے قائم مقام ہے اور جو چیز کسی شی ء نے قائم مقام ہو ممکن نہیں کہ وہ من کل وجہ اس کے معنی میں ہو ورنہ تو وہ عین شی ہوگی نہ کہ قائم مقام ۔ پس مہینہ کا قائم مقام ہونا صرف عدت گزارنے اور استبراء کیلئے ہے نہ کہ کسی اور اعتبار۔ لہذا اب یہ اشکال واقع نہیں ہوگا کہ جب مہینہ حیض کے قائم مقام ہے تو مہینہ میں طلاق واقع کرنا حیض میں واقع کرنا ہے۔ کیونکہ طلاق واقع کرنے میں مہینہ حیض کے قائم مقام نہیں ہے۔ دوسرے اشکال کا جواب یہ ہے کہ شریعت نے مہینوں کو حیض کے قائم مقام اسلئے بنایا تاکہ ان کے ذریعہ عورت عدت گزار سکے۔ اور عدت بالعموم تین ماہ میں پوری ہوتی ہے۔ اس وجہ سے مہینوں کو ان حیض کے قائم مقام کیا گیا جن میں عدت پائی جاتی تھی اور مدت حیض کے قائم مقام نہیں کیا گیا یہاں تک کہ ایک ماہ پر اکتفاء کیا جاتا۔ پس جب یہ ثابت ہو گیا کہ مہینہ حیض کے قائم مقام ہے تو اب اگر ایقاع طلاق مہینہ کے شروع میں ہے تو وہ مہینے جو حیض کے قائم مقام ہیں ان کا اعتبار چاندوں کے ذریعہ ہو گا یعنی پورے تین ماہ عدت گزارے چاند ۲۹ کا ہو یا ۳۰ کا۔ اور اگر ایقاع طلاق مہینہ کے درمیان میں ہے تو تین طلاق متفرق طور سے دینے میں مہینوں کا اعتبار ایام کے ذریعہ ہوگا نہ کہ چاند کے ذریعہ (یہ مسئلہ متفق علیہ ہے ) تفصیل یہ ہے کہ طلاق سنت کی صورت میں دوسری طلاق ۳۰ دن پورے ہونے کے بعد اکتیسویں دن میں واقع کرے۔ اسلئے کہ ہر ماہ تیس دن کا معتبر ہے۔ چنانچہ جس روز ۳۰ دن پورے ہو رہے ہیں۔ اگر اس روز طلاق واقع کی تو ایک ماہ میں دو طلاق جمع کرنے والا ہوگا۔ اور عدت کے حق میں بھی امام صاحب کے نزدیک ایام ہی معتبر ہیں۔ لہذا عورت کی عدت نوے دن گزرنے سے پوری ہوگی ۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک جس ماہ کے وسط میں طلاق دی گئی اس کو پورا کیا جائے آخر ماہ کے ساتھ اور درمیان کے دو ماہ میں چاند معتبر ہے۔ مثلاً ایک شخص نے اپنی بیوی کو چاند کی ۱۵ تاریخ میں طلاق دی اور یہ مہینہ ۲۹ کا ہوا تو ۴ دن اس ماہ کے اور ۶ دن آخری ماہ کے اور درمیان کے دو ماہ چاند کے حساب سے معتبر ہوں گے۔ مہینہ ۲۹ کا ہو یا ۳۰ کا یہ مسئلہ اصل میں اجارات کا ہے۔ یعنی اگر تین ماہ کیلئے مہینہ کے بالکل شروع میں مکان کرایہ پر لیا تو بالاتفاق تین ماہ چاندوں کے ذریعہ معتبر ہوں گے۔ چاند ۲۹ کا ہو یا ۳۰ کا۔ اور اگر درمیان ماہ میں کرایہ پر لیا ہے تو امام صاحب کے نزدیک تین ماہ کا اعتبار ایام کے ذریعہ ہوگا۔ یعنی نوے دن اور صاحبین کے نزدیک اول ماہ پورا کیا جائے گا آخر ماہ کے ساتھ بذریعہ ایام کے۔ اور درمیان کے دوماہ چاند کے ذریعہ پورے کیئے جائیں۔ کہا گیا کہ فتویٰ صاحبین کے قول پر ہے۔ فوائد عورت کا من حیض مختار مذہب کی بناء پر 9 سال ہے اور بعض کے نزدیک ۸ سال اور بعض کے نزدیک ۷ سال ہے اور سن ایاس قول اظہر کی بناء پر ۵۵ سال ہے۔ (فتح القدير مع الکفایہ ) واللہ اعلم بالصواب
Likewise, according to Abu Hanifa, while according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the first is completed by the last, and the middle two by lunar months, and this is the issue of leases. Translation: Al-Quduri said: When a woman does not menstruate due to youth or old age, then he intends to give her three divorces at the time of sunnah, he should give one divorce. Then when one month passes, he gives the second divorce. Because the month stands in place of menstruation for both. Allah said: 'And those who have despaired of menstruation... and those who have not menstruated.' And substitution is specific to menstruation, so that for both, istibra' is estimated by month, even though istibra' is by menstruation. If in the middle of the month, then for the purpose of separation it will be by days. Similarly for 'iddah. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, and according to the two, the first is completed by the last, and the middle two months by lunar months. And this issue pertains to leases. Explanation: If a woman does not menstruate due to youth or old age, and her husband wants to give her three divorces in the sunnah way, the ruling is that he gives three divorces separately over three months. The proof is that the month stands in place of menstruation for both young and old, because Allah said: 'And those who have despaired of menstruation from your women, if you doubt, their 'iddah is three months, and those who have not menstruated.' This indicates that if they menstruated, their 'iddah would be three menstruations, but since they do not menstruate, their 'iddah is three months. So it is established that the month substitutes for menstruation. 'And substitution in menstruation' - the chosen madhhab of the Hanafis is that the month specifically substitutes for menstruation, not for both menstruation and purity, as some others hold. Shams al-A'imma said some hold that for non-menstruating women the month is in place of menstruation, but for menstruating women it is in place of purity, but this is not correct; for them too the month is in place of menstruation. The proof of the chosen madhhab is that a slave girl who does not menstruate due to youth or old age - if istibra' is required due to transfer of ownership etc., that istibra' is estimated by month, even though istibra' is by menstruation, not by purity. So this also proves that the month only substitutes for menstruation, not for both. On this presentation, an objection arises: If the month substitutes for menstruation, whenever he divorces in any of these months, that divorce would be during menstruation, and that is prohibited as in the state of menstruation. A second objection: If the month substitutes for menstruation, why is three months needed for three menstruations? Since the maximum duration of menstruation is ten days, and the period of three menstruations could be completed in one month, so one month should substitute for three menstruations, not three months. The answer to the first objection: This period (month) is essentially purity, but it substitutes for menstruation. Anything that substitutes for something else cannot be identical in every aspect, otherwise it would be the same thing, not a substitute. So the substitution of the month is only for the purpose of completing 'iddah and istibra', not for any other purpose. Therefore, this objection does not arise that divorcing in the month is divorcing during menstruation, because the month does not substitute for menstruation in the ruling of divorce. The answer to the second objection: Shari'ah made months substitutes for menstruation so that the woman can complete her 'iddah through them. And 'iddah is generally completed in three months. So months were made substitutes for those menstruations in which 'iddah is found, not for the duration of menstruation such that one month would suffice. So when it is established that the month substitutes for menstruation, then if the divorce is at the beginning of a month, the months that substitute for menstruation are counted by lunar months, i.e., she completes three months of 'iddah whether the month is 29 or 30 days. If the divorce is in the middle of a month, then for giving three divorces separately, months are counted by days, not by lunar months (this issue is agreed upon). Details: In the case of sunnah divorce, the second divorce should be given after 30 days have passed, on the 31st day, because each month is considered to be 30 days. Thus, if he gives divorce on the day when 30 days are completed, he would be combining two divorces in one month. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, for 'iddah, days are considered, so the woman's 'iddah will be completed after 90 days. According to the two, if the divorce is given in the middle of the month, that month is completed by the last month by days, and the middle two months by lunar months. Example: A man gave divorce to his wife on the 15th of the lunar month, and that month was 29 days; then 4 days of that month and 6 days of the last month, and the middle two months will be counted by lunar months. Whether the month is 29 or 30 days, this issue originates from leases. That is, if a house is rented for three months starting exactly at the beginning of a month, then by agreement three months are counted by lunar months, whether 29 or 30 days. If rented in the middle of a month, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the three months are counted by days, i.e., 90 days; according to the two, the first month is completed by the last month by days, and the middle two months are completed by lunar months. It is said that the fatwa is according to the two. Benefits: The minimum age of menstruation according to the chosen madhhab is 9 years, some say 8, some say 7; the age of despair (senility) according to the more apparent view is 55 years. (Fath al-Qadir with al-Kifayah) And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 229

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the ruling on divorcing a woman who does not menstruate due to youth or old age, and the method of counting months for 'iddah and istibra'. The author first presents the matn from Al-Quduri which states that according to Abu Hanifa, the first month (when divorce occurs in the middle) is completed by the last month, and the middle two months by lunar months, while according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the first month is completed by the last month and the middle two by lunar months. The commentary then explains that the month substitutes for menstruation for both young and old women, based on Quran 65:4. The Hanafi chosen madhhab holds that the month specifically substitutes for menstruation, not purity, as evidenced by the ruling of istibra' for a slave girl. Two objections are raised and answered: (1) if month substitutes for menstruation, then divorcing in that month would be like divorcing during menstruation which is haram; the answer: the substitution is only for 'iddah and istibra', not for the ruling of divorce. (2) why three months instead of one month to substitute for three menstruations; the answer: months substitute for the entire 'iddah period which is three months, not for the duration of menstruation. Then the details of counting: if divorce at beginning of month, use lunar months; if in middle, use days (30 days per month) according to Abu Hanifa, while Sahibayn say the first month is completed with the last month by days, and middle two by lunar months. The fatwa is on the Sahibayn's view. Finally, benefits about the minimum age of menstruation (9 years) and age of despair (55 years). This shows the precision of Hanafi fiqh in dealing with exceptional cases.

Key Terms
قائم مقام (qa'im maqam): Something that stands in the place of another thing, serving the same legal purpose.
استبراء (istibra'): A waiting period to verify that a slave girl is not pregnant after change of ownership.
عدت ('iddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after divorce or death of husband before remarrying.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi chosen madhhab, what is the minimum age of menstruation?
A) 7 years
B) 8 years
C) 9 years
D) 10 years

Key Takeaway
For a non-menstruating woman, her 'iddah is three months; if divorce occurs mid-month, the mufta bihi Hanafi position counts the first month by days and the middle two by lunar months.

Ruling on Separating Intercourse and Divorce: Imam Zufar's View
Presents the ruling on whether a waiting period is required between intercourse and divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi majority's position on the necessity of a waiting period (fasl) between intercourse and divorce for non-menstruating women, explain Imam Zufar's contrary view, and evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
No fasl needed when pregnancy is impossible; Zufar's month analogy fails because desire renews differently.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether a husband must wait a period of time between intercourse and divorce when divorcing a woman who does not menstruate (young or old). The majority of the Hanafi school, including Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani, hold that no such waiting period is required. Imam Zufar, however, argues for a one-month separation. By analyzing the proofs on both sides, you will understand the legal reasoning that leads to the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
State the majority position and its basis
Identify the ruling as presented in the matn: no separation required. Note the key reason: pregnancy is not suspected in non-menstruating women.
The matn is from Al-Quduri, stating permissibility.
2
Identify Zufar's position and his dalil
Zufar requires a month's separation. His proof: the month substitutes for menstruation, and desire diminishes after intercourse, requiring a month to renew.
Zufar draws an analogy with menstruating women.
3
Follow the Hanafi response to Zufar's argument
The majority responds: the dislike for menstruating women is due to confusion over 'iddah, which does not apply when pregnancy is impossible. Additionally, desire may decrease in one aspect but increases from another (desire for intercourse without child expenses).
The majority uses a two-pronged counter-argument.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: according to Zufar, one must wait a month; according to the majority, no wait is required. The majority view is mufta bihi.
The dispute affects actual divorce practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ويجوزان يطلقها ولا يفصل بين وطيها وطلاقها بزمان وقال زفر يفصل بينهما بشهر لقيامه مقام الحيض ولان بالجماع تفتر الرغبة وانما تتجدد بزمان وهو الشهر ولنا انه لايتوهم الحبل فيهما والكراهية فى ذوات الحيض باعتباره لان عند ذلك يشتبه وجه العدة والرغبة وان كانت تفتر من الوجه الذى ذكر لكن تكثر من وجه اخر لانه يرغب فى وطى غير معلق فرارا عن مؤن الولد فكان الزمان زمان الرغبة فصار كزمان الحبل ترجمہ قدوری نے کہا کہ جائز ہے کہ اسکو طلاق ہے اور اس کی وطی اور طلاق میں کسی زمانہ کا فصل نہ کرے اور امام زفر نے فرمایا کہ ایک ماہ کا فصل کرے کیونکہ ماہ حیض کے قائم مقام ہے۔ اور اس لئے کہ جماع کی وجہ سے رغبت کم ہو جاتی ہے اور نئی ہوگی ایک زمانہ سے مراد وہ ماہ ہے۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ صغیرہ اور آیسہ کے حق میں حمل متوہم نہیں ہے اور ذوات الحیض میں کراہت اسی اعتبار سے تھی۔
He (Al-Quduri) said: It is permissible for him to divorce her without separating between intercourse and divorce by any period. Zufar said: He should separate between them by a month, because the month stands in place of menstruation, and because through intercourse desire diminishes and only renews over time, which is a month. Our proof: that pregnancy is not suspected in them (young or old), and the dislike (karahah) in menstruating women is due to the fact that then the matter of 'iddah is confused. And even though desire diminishes from the mentioned aspect, it increases from another aspect: because he desires intercourse without attachment to avoid the expenses of a child, so the time is one of desire, thus it becomes like the time of pregnancy. Translation: Al-Quduri said: It is permissible for him to divorce her and not separate between her intercourse and divorce by any period. Imam Zufar said: He should separate by a month, because the month stands in place of menstruation, and because through intercourse desire diminishes and only renews over time, meaning a month. Our proof: that in the young and old woman, pregnancy is not suspected, and the dislike in menstruating women was due to that, because then the face of 'iddah is confused. And even though desire diminishes from the aspect mentioned, it increases from another aspect: because he desires intercourse that is not attached (to pregnancy) to avoid the expenses of a child, so the time is one of desire, thus it becomes like the time of pregnancy.
Source pages p. 230

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between the majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) and Imam Zufar regarding whether a waiting period is required between intercourse and divorce. The matn from Al-Quduri states that it is permissible to divorce immediately after intercourse without any separation, and this is the position of the Hanafi school. Imam Zufar, however, argues that a month's separation is required. His reasoning: the month stands in place of menstruation, and after intercourse, desire diminishes and needs time to renew. The Hanafi majority responds: for young and old women who do not menstruate, pregnancy is not expected, so there is no need for a waiting period to establish 'iddah. The prohibition (karahah) for menstruating women is due to the confusion about 'iddah, which does not apply here. Additionally, even if desire diminishes from one aspect, it increases from another: the man desires intercourse without the burden of a child, so the time is actually one of desire, not lack thereof. Therefore, no separation is required. The relied-upon view is that of the majority.

Key Terms
فصل (fasl): A separation or interval of time between intercourse and divorce.
رغبت (raghbah): Desire for intercourse; the text discusses how it diminishes and renews.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the key reason the Hanafi majority gives for not requiring a waiting period after intercourse for a non-menstruating woman?
A) The month does not substitute for menstruation in any case
B) Pregnancy is not suspected in such women
C) The woman's desire is always present
D) The man's desire always remains high

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school does not require a waiting period after intercourse for divorce when the woman does not menstruate, because pregnancy is impossible and the analogy with menstruation fails.

Divorcing Non-Menstruating Women Immediately After Intercourse
Ruling with proof: permissibility of immediate divorce for ayyisa/saghira

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on divorcing an ayyisa or saghira immediately after intercourse and explain why no interval is required.

Core Idea
No interval needed for ayyisa/saghira — pregnancy impossible, so iddah ambiguity absent.

This passage addresses a nuance in divorce law: whether a husband must wait before divorcing his wife after intercourse when she is not menstruating. The Hanafi school distinguishes between women who menstruate and those who do not, based on the possibility of pregnancy. The matn from Al-Quduri permits immediate divorce, while Imam Zufar argues for a one-month interval. Understanding the illa (effective cause) is key to resolving the dispute.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling in the matn
Al-Quduri states it is permissible to divorce without any time separation after intercourse. This is the starting point.
2
Locate the opponent's position
Imam Zufar requires a one-month interval, analogizing to menstruating women where a month replaces a menstruation.
Zufar is within the Hanafi school but his view is marjuh.
3
Analyze the opponent's proof
Zufar's proof: (1) Month replaces menstruation by analogy; (2) Intercourse diminishes desire, needing a month to rekindle.
This is a qiyas-based argument.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response (lana)
The Hanafi proof: Pregnancy is impossible in ayyisa/saghira, so the reason for dislike in menstruating women (iddah ambiguity) is absent. Desire actually increases due to freedom from child expenses, so the time resembles that of a pregnant woman where immediate divorce is allowed.
The illa is the possibility of pregnancy, not desire alone.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and tarjih
Practical difference: immediate divorce vs. one month wait. The Hanafi position (no interval) is mufta bihi and supported by the majority of scholars including the other three Sunni schools.
The tarjih is based on the strength of the illa analysis.

Source Text

قال ويجوزان يطلقها ولا يفصل بين وطيها وطلاقها بزمان وقال زفر يفصل بينهما بشهر لقيامه مقام الحيض ولان بالجماع تفتر الرغبة وانما تتجدد بزمان وهو الشهر ولنا انه لايتوهم الحبل فيهما والكراهية فى ذوات الحيض باعتباره لان عند ذلك يشتبه وجه العدة والرغبة وان كانت تفتر من الوجه الذى ذكر لكن تكثر من وجه اخر لانه يرغب فى وطى غير معلق فرارا عن مؤن الولد فكان الزمان زمان الرغبة فصار كزمان الحبل
ترجمہ قدوری نے کہا کہ جائز ہے کہ اسکو طلاق ہے اور اس کی وطی اور طلاق میں کسی زمانہ کا فصل نہ کرے اور امام زفر نے فرمایا کہ ایک ماہ کا فصل کرے کیونکہ ماہ حیض کے قائم مقام ہے۔ اور اس لئے کہ جماع کی وجہ سے رغبت کم ہو جاتی ہے اور نئی ہوگی ایک زمانہ سے مراد وہ ماہ ہے۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ صغیرہ اور آنسہ کے حق میں حمل متوہم نہیں ہے اور ذوات الحیض میں کراہت اسی اعتبار سے تھی۔
تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ آئسہ اور صغیرہ کو طلاق دینا درانحالیکہ اس کی طلاق اور ولی کے درمیان زمانے کے ساتھ فصل نہ کیا جائے جائز ہے۔ یہی قول امام مالک، امام شافعی اور امام احمد کا ہے اور امام زفر نے فرمایا کہ اس کی وطی اور طلاق میں ایک ماہ کا فصل ضروری ہے۔ امام زفر کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ماہ حیض کے قائم مقام ہے اور ذوات الحیض میں وطی اور طلاق کے درمیان ایک حیض کا فصل ضروری تھا۔ لہذا غیر ذوات الحیض میں بھی ایک ماہ کا فصل ضروری ہوگا۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ جماع کی وجہ سے رغبت کم ہو جاتی ہے۔ (عادة ) جیسے کہ ذوات الحیض میں جب طہر میں ولی کرلی گئی تو رغبت کم ہو جاتی ہے اور تجد در غبت کیلئے ایک مدت درکار ہے۔ لہذا ولی اور اس کی طلاق کے درمیان اس قدر مدت کا فصل ضروری ہے۔ جس سے تجد در غبت ہو جائے اور وہ مدت ایک ماہ ہے۔ اس وجہ سے امام زفر کی رائے یہ ہے کہ آئیسہ اور صغیرہ کی وطی اور طلاق میں ایک ماہ کا فضل ضروری ہے، جیسا کہ ذوات الحیض میں ایک حیض کا فصل ضروی تھا۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ ذوات الحیض میں طلاق بعد الجماع کی کراہت تو ہم عمل کی وجہ سے تھی ، کیونکہ تو ہم حمل کے وقت عدت مشتبہ ہو جاتی ہے۔ معلوم نہیں ہو سکے گا کہ وہ حاملہ ہے تا کہ عدت وضع حمل ہو یا غیر حاملہ کہ اس کی عدت تین حیض ہوں۔ بہر حال جب ذوات الحیض میں طلاق بعد الجماع کی کراہت تو ہم حمل کی وجہ سے تھی ۔ اور آئیسہ اور صغیرہ میں تو ہم حمل کی کوئی گنجائش نہیں لہذا ان دونوں کے حق میں طلاق بعد الجماع بھی بلا کراہت مباح ہوگی۔ ولی اور طلاق کے درمیان فصل کی چنداں ضرورت نہیں رہی۔ اور رہا امام زفر کا یہ کہنا کہ جماع سے رغبت کم ہو جاتی ہے تسلیم ہے۔ لیکن امام زفر کی بیان کردہ وجہ کے اعتبار سے اگر چہ رغبت کم ہو جاتی ہے مگر دوسرے اعتبار سے رغبت زیادہ ہو جاتی ہے۔ کیونکہ آئسہ اور صغیرہ سے جو دلی کی جائے گی اس سے علوق نہیں ہو گا یعنی حاملہ نہیں ہوگی۔ اور اولاد کے خرچ سے بچنے کیلئے انسان ایسی وطی میں رغبت کرتا ہے جو غیر معلق ہو یعنی حاملہ بنانے والی نہ ہو۔ پس معلوم ہو گیا کہ آئیسہ اور صغیرہ کے حق میں جامع کے فورا بعد کا زمانہ بھی رغبت کا زمانہ ہے۔ پس حاملہ کے زمانے کے مشابہ ہو گیا۔ کیونکہ حاملہ عورت کو بھی جماع کے بعد بلافصل طلاق دینا جائز ہے۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب۔
He (Al-Quduri) said: It is permissible for him to divorce her without separating between intercourse and divorce by any time. Zufar said: He should separate between them by a month, because the month takes the place of menstruation, and because through intercourse desire diminishes, and it only renews after a time, which is the month. Our proof: Pregnancy is not conceivable in these two (the old woman and the young girl), and the dislike in menstruating women was because of that consideration, because then the basis of the waiting period becomes ambiguous. And desire, even if it diminishes from the aspect mentioned, but increases from another aspect: because he desires intercourse that is not productive (of pregnancy), fleeing from the expenses of a child. So this time is a time of desire, and it becomes like the time of pregnancy. Translation: Al-Quduri said: It is permissible to divorce her and not separate between her intercourse and divorce by any time. Imam Zufar said: He should separate by a month, because the month takes the place of menstruation, and because through intercourse desire diminishes and renews after a time, meaning that month. Our proof: In the case of a young girl and an old woman, pregnancy is not conceivable, and the dislike in menstruating women was on that basis. Explanation: The issue is that divorcing an ayyisa (old woman) or saghira (young girl) without separating between her intercourse and divorce by time is permissible. This is the ruling of Imam Malik, Imam Shafi'i, and Imam Ahmad. Imam Zufar said: A separation of one month between intercourse and divorce is necessary. Imam Zufar's proof: The month takes the place of menstruation, and in menstruating women a separation of one menstruation between intercourse and divorce was necessary, so in non-menstruating women a month's separation is necessary. Second proof: Through intercourse desire diminishes, as is customary, like in menstruating women when intercourse occurs in purity, desire diminishes, and for renewal of desire a period is needed. So a separation of that amount of time is necessary between intercourse and divorce, and that period is one month. For this reason, Imam Zufar's opinion is that for an ayyisa and saghira, a month's separation between intercourse and divorce is necessary, just as a menstruation's separation was necessary in menstruating women. Our proof: The dislike of divorce after intercourse in menstruating women was due to the possibility of pregnancy, because at the time of pregnancy the waiting period becomes ambiguous. It cannot be known whether she is pregnant so her waiting period is delivery, or not pregnant so her waiting period is three menstruations. In any case, since the dislike in menstruating women after intercourse was due to the possibility of pregnancy, and in ayyisa and saghira there is no possibility of pregnancy, therefore for these two, divorce after intercourse is permissible without dislike. There is no need for a separation between intercourse and divorce. As for Imam Zufar's statement that desire diminishes through intercourse, it is accepted. But according to the reason mentioned by Zufar, even if desire diminishes in one aspect, it increases in another aspect. Because intercourse with an ayyisa or saghira will not result in pregnancy, and to avoid the expenses of children, a person desires intercourse that is not productive. So it is understood that for ayyisa and saghira, the time immediately after intercourse is also a time of desire. So it resembles the time of a pregnant woman. Because divorcing a pregnant woman immediately after intercourse is also permissible. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 230

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab and intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the necessity of a time interval between intercourse and divorce for women who do not menstruate (ayyisa: post-menopausal; saghira: pre-pubescent). The matn from Al-Quduri states that no separation is required. Imam Zufar, a Hanafi scholar, disagrees and requires a month. His reasoning is qiyas (analogy) to menstruating women, where a separation of one menstruation is required when divorcing after intercourse to avoid ambiguity about the waiting period. He also argues that intercourse reduces desire, and a month is needed for desire to rekindle. The Hanafi response (presented as 'lana' – our proof) distinguishes between menstruating and non-menstruating women: the dislike in menstruating women is due to the possibility of pregnancy, which makes the waiting period uncertain. Since ayyisa and saghira cannot become pregnant, there is no such ambiguity, so divorce immediately after intercourse is permissible. Regarding desire, the Hanafi position acknowledges it diminishes but claims it increases from another perspective: men desire non-productive intercourse to avoid child expenses, so the time after intercourse is actually a time of desire, analogous to a pregnant woman. The relied-upon Hanafi position is that no interval is required, and this is also the position of the other three Sunni schools.

Key Terms
آئسہ (ayyisa): A woman who has reached menopause and no longer menstruates.
صغیرہ (saghira): A young girl who has not yet reached puberty and does not menstruate.
ذوات الحیض (dhawat al-hayd): Women who menstruate regularly.
ولی (wat'): Sexual intercourse with the wife.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, is it permissible to divorce an ayyisa (post-menopausal woman) immediately after intercourse without any interval?
A) No, it is makruh.
B) Yes, it is permissible.
C) Only after one month.
D) Only after one menstruation.

Key Takeaway
Divorcing a non-menstruating woman immediately after intercourse is permissible because there is no pregnancy risk to confuse the iddah.

Talaq — Divorce

Divorcing a Pregnant Woman After Intercourse
Ruling on divorcing a pregnant woman right after intercourse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on divorcing a pregnant woman immediately after intercourse and explain the legal reasoning (illah) behind its permissibility.

Core Idea
A pregnant woman can be divorced right after intercourse because her iddah is certain and no pregnancy ambiguity arises.

The general rule in Hanafi fiqh is that divorcing a woman immediately after intercourse is disliked (makruh) due to potential confusion about her iddah. However, an exception is made when the woman is pregnant. Why does the school permit what is otherwise discouraged? The key lies in the certainty of the iddah period for a pregnant woman. In this lesson, we unpack the rational proof (dalil aqli) that leads to this ruling and understand its practical application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act
The act under discussion is divorcing a pregnant woman immediately after sexual intercourse. Note that the ruling concerns the timing of the divorce, not the validity of divorce itself.
The act is a subcase of the broader category of talaq.
2
Recall the General Rule
For a non-pregnant woman, divorcing immediately after intercourse is makruh (disliked) because it creates ambiguity about her iddah—whether it should be counted by menstrual cycles or by a potential pregnancy from that intercourse.
This baseline helps highlight the exception.
3
Extract the Illah (Legal Reason)
The text gives two reasons: (a) Divorcing a pregnant woman does not lead to confusion about the type of iddah, because her iddah ends definitively with delivery; (b) The time of pregnancy is a time of desire for intercourse, so intercourse does not diminish desire. The primary illah is the certainty of iddah.
The second reason reinforces why the karahah is removed.
4
Contrast with Non-Pregnant Case
The absence of iddah ambiguity is the distinguishing factor. For a non-pregnant woman, intercourse could result in pregnancy, making the basis of iddah unclear (menstrual cycles vs. delivery). For a pregnant woman, no such uncertainty exists.
This is a clear example of tanqih al-manat (refining the effective cause).
5
Apply the Principle
The rule derived: Whenever the iddah is clear and unambiguous, divorce immediately after intercourse is permissible. Thus, a pregnant woman may be divorced at any time, even right after intercourse.
This principle can be extended to other cases where iddah is determined by an unambiguous event.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وطلاق الحـامـل يـجـوز عـقـيـب الجماع لانه لا يودى الى اشتباه وجه العدة و زمان الحبل زمان الرغبة في الوطى لكونه غير معلق اوفيها لمكان ولده منها فلايقل الرغبة بالجماع
ترجمہ جماع کے بعد حاملہ (عورت) کو طلاق دینا جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ عدت کے طریقہ کے مشتبہ ہونے کا سبب نہیں ہوگا۔ اور حمل کا زمانہ دہلی میں رغبت کا زمانہ ہے اسلئے کہ یہ ولی غیر متعلق ہے۔ یا حاملہ عورت میں (اسلئے رغبت ہے ) کہ اس حاملہ سے اس کا ولد ممکن الوجود ہے۔ پس جماع کی وجہ سے رغبت کم نہیں ہوگی۔
تشریح مسئلہ ... حاملہ عورت کے ساتھ ولی اور طلاق کے درمیان بھی فصل ضروری نہیں ہے۔ بلکہ حاملہ عورت کو جماع کے بعد طلاق
And divorce of a pregnant woman is permissible immediately after intercourse, because it does not lead to ambiguity of the basis of the waiting period, and the time of pregnancy is a time of desire for intercourse because it is not productive (of pregnancy), or in her (the pregnant woman) because of the existence of her child from him, so desire is not diminished by intercourse. Translation: Divorcing a pregnant woman after intercourse is permissible, because it will not cause ambiguity regarding the waiting period. And the time of pregnancy is a time of desire for intercourse because it is non-productive, or in a pregnant woman there is desire because her child from him is possible of existence. So desire will not decrease due to intercourse. Explanation: The issue... For a pregnant woman, there is no need for separation between intercourse and divorce. Rather, divorcing a pregnant woman after intercourse.
Source pages p. 231

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling concerning the divorce of a pregnant woman. The text states that it is permissible to divorce a pregnant woman immediately after sexual intercourse. The reasoning is twofold: first, there is no ambiguity regarding the waiting period (iddah) because the waiting period for a pregnant woman is until she gives birth, which is clear regardless of when the divorce occurs. Second, the time of pregnancy is a time of desire for intercourse because the intercourse will not result in additional pregnancy (since she is already pregnant), or because the child is already present, so the desire does not diminish after intercourse. This contrasts with menstruating women, where the possibility of pregnancy creates ambiguity about the iddah, and therefore immediate divorce after intercourse is disliked. The passage affirms that a pregnant woman can be divorced at any time, even immediately after intercourse, without any waiting period between the act and the pronouncement of divorce.

Key Terms
حاملہ (hamila): A pregnant woman.
عدت (iddah): The waiting period after divorce or death of husband.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is it permissible to divorce a pregnant woman immediately after intercourse?
A) Because she has no iddah.
B) Because there is no ambiguity about her iddah, which ends with delivery.
C) Because she is not menstruating.
D) Because the husband's desire is renewed instantly.

Key Takeaway
Divorcing a pregnant woman immediately after intercourse is permissible because the iddah is certain, eliminating the ambiguity that makes it disliked for non-pregnant women.

Talaq — Divorce

Divorce of Post-Menopausal or Minor Wife: The Waiting Period Dispute
Resolves dispute on divorcing ayisa/saghira without waiting period

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi majority position on divorcing an ayisa or saghira immediately after intercourse and explain why Imam Zufar's objection is not accepted.

Core Idea
No waiting period is needed because pregnancy is impossible, removing the reason for delay.

This passage addresses a specific dispute within the Hanafi school regarding the permissibility of divorcing a wife who does not menstruate (ayisa or saghira) immediately after intercourse. Imam Zufar analogizes to menstruating women, requiring a one-month gap, but the majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) and the three other Imams hold it permissible without any delay. We will examine the reasoning on both sides to understand the legal principle at work.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Categories of Wives
The passage discusses two types of wives: the ayisa (post-menopausal) and the saghira (pre-pubescent minor). Both are characterized by the absence of menstruation, so the usual rules for divorce timing (based on menstrual cycles) do not apply directly.
2
Understand Imam Zufar's Qiyas
Imam Zufar argues that a one-month separation is necessary, drawing an analogy to menstruating women. For them, a separation of one menstrual period (or a state of purity) is recommended/required to avoid confusion about pregnancy. Zufar treats the month as a substitute for a menstrual period, and also claims that intercourse reduces desire, so a month is needed to renew it.
His argument relies on two points: the month as substitute for tuhr, and the need to renew desire.
3
Analyze the Hanafi Majority Response
The Hanafi majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) refute the qiyas by pointing out that the underlying cause (illa) for the rule in menstruating women is the possibility of pregnancy causing iddah confusion. Since ayisa and saghira cannot become pregnant, the cause is absent, and the rule does not apply. Furthermore, they argue that desire may actually increase because such intercourse is free from the risk of pregnancy and its expenses.
The majority also note that this position aligns with Imam Malik, al-Shafi'i, and Ahmad ibn Hanbal.
4
Determine the Practical Ruling (Mufta Bihi)
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that no waiting period is required; divorce immediately after intercourse is permissible (mubah) without any dislike. This is based on the absence of the effective cause and supported by the fact that many scholars outside the Hanafi school also hold this view.
Imam Zufar's view is considered a minority position within the Hanafi school and is not followed in fatwa.

بعد الجماع بھی بلا کراہت مباح ہوگی۔ ولی اور طلاق کے درمیان فصل کی چنداں ضرورت نہیں رہی۔ اور رہا امام زفر کا یہ کہنا کہ جماع سے رغبت کم ہو جاتی ہے تسلیم ہے۔ لیکن امام زفر کی بیان کردہ وجہ کے اعتبار سے اگر چہ رغبت کم ہو جاتی ہے مگر دوسرے اعتبار سے رغبت زیادہ ہو جاتی ہے۔ کیونکہ آئسہ اور صغیرہ سے جو دلی کی جائے گی اس سے علوق نہیں ہو گا یعنی حاملہ نہیں ہوگی۔ اور اولاد کے خرچ سے بچنے کیلئے انسان ایسی وطی میں رغبت کرتا ہے جو غیر معلق ہو یعنی حاملہ بنانے والی نہ ہو۔ پس معلوم ہو گیا کہ آئیسہ اور صغیرہ کے حق میں جامع کے فورا بعد کا زمانہ بھی رغبت کا زمانہ ہے۔ پس حاملہ کے زمانے کے مشابہ ہو گیا۔ کیونکہ حاملہ عورت کو بھی جماع کے بعد بلافصل طلاق دینا جائز ہے۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب۔ جمیل احمد سکروڈ وی۔
Book of Divorce 330 Ashraf al-Hidaya Urdu Commentary on Hidaya Volume Four Because at that time the method of iddah would become ambiguous. And desire, although it decreases for the reason mentioned by Imam Zufar, but due to another reason it will increase. Because a man desires intercourse that does not result in pregnancy, fleeing from the expense of children. So this is a time of desire, and it became like the time of pregnancy. Explanation: The issue is that divorcing an ayisa (post-menopausal) and a saghira (minor) is permissible without separating between the divorce and intercourse with a period of time. This is the saying of Imam Malik, Imam Shafi'i, and Imam Ahmad. Imam Zufar said that there must be a separation of one month between intercourse and divorce. Imam Zufar's evidence is that a month is a substitute for a menstrual period, and for menstruating women, separation of one menstrual period between intercourse and divorce was necessary. Therefore, for non-menstruating women as well, separation of one month will be necessary. His second evidence is that intercourse reduces desire. Customarily, just as when intercourse occurs in a state of purity (tuhr) for menstruating women, desire decreases, and for renewal of desire a period is needed. So between intercourse and its divorce, separation of a period that renews desire is necessary, and that period is one month. For this reason, Imam Zufar's opinion is that for an ayisa and a saghira, separation of one month between intercourse and divorce is necessary, just as for menstruating women separation of one menstrual period was necessary. Our evidence is: For menstruating women, the dislike of divorce after intercourse was due to the possibility of pregnancy, because pregnancy makes the iddah period ambiguous. It cannot be known whether she is pregnant so that her iddah is until delivery, or not pregnant so that her iddah is three menstruations. In any case, when for menstruating women the dislike of divorce after intercourse was due to the possibility of pregnancy, and for an ayisa and a saghira there is no possibility of pregnancy, therefore for these two, divorce after intercourse without dislike is permissible. There is no need for separation between intercourse and divorce. As for Imam Zufar's saying that intercourse reduces desire, it is admitted. But according to the reason mentioned by Imam Zufar, although desire decreases, from another aspect desire increases. Because intercourse with an ayisa and a saghira will not result in pregnancy, and to avoid the expense of children, a man desires intercourse that is non-procreative. So it became clear that for an ayisa and a saghira, the time immediately after intercourse is also a time of desire. Thus it resembles the time of pregnancy, because for a pregnant woman also, divorce immediately after intercourse is permissible. And Allah knows best. Jameel Ahmad Sakrodi.
Source pages p. 231

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Zufar and the majority of Hanafi scholars (as well as other schools) regarding divorcing a post-menopausal (ayisa) or minor (saghira) wife immediately after intercourse. The majority (including Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and the three other school founders) hold it permissible without any waiting period. Imam Zufar requires a one-month separation. The text presents Zufar's arguments: the month substitutes for a menstrual period, and intercourse reduces desire, so a month is needed to renew desire. The Hanafi response is that the prohibition for menstruating women was due to potential confusion of iddah from pregnancy, which is absent here. Moreover, desire may actually increase because such intercourse does not lead to pregnancy, so a man may desire it. The ruling is that divorce immediately after intercourse is permissible (mubah) without dislike.

Key Terms
آئسہ (āyisa): A post-menopausal woman who no longer menstruates.
صغیرہ (saghīra): A minor girl who has not yet reached puberty (and thus does not menstruate).
فصل (faṣl): Separation or interval of time between two events (here, between intercourse and divorce).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi position, what is the ruling on divorcing a post-menopausal woman (ayisa) immediately after intercourse without any waiting period?
A) Haram
B) Makruh Tahrimi
C) Mubah (permissible without dislike)
D) Wajib

Key Takeaway
Divorcing a post-menopausal or minor wife immediately after intercourse is permissible without any waiting period, because the reason for delay (pregnancy confusion) does not exist.
